###begin article-title 0
###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
Molecular evolution of Phox-related regulatory subunits for NADPH oxidase enzymes
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
This is an Open Access article distributed under the terms of the Creative Commons Attribution License (), which permits unrestricted use, distribution, and reproduction in any medium, provided the original work is properly cited.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Background
###end title 2
###begin p 3
###xml 31 32 31 32 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</underline>
###xml 37 39 37 39 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ox</underline>
###xml 409 413 409 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 472 476 472 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 481 485 481 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 490 495 490 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 642 647 642 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 654 658 654 658 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 677 682 677 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 753 758 753 758 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 808 812 808 812 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
The reactive oxygen-generating NADPH oxidases (Noxes) function in a variety of biological roles, and can be broadly classified into those that are regulated by subunit interactions and those that are regulated by calcium. The prototypical subunit-regulated Nox, Nox2, is the membrane-associated catalytic subunit of the phagocyte NADPH-oxidase. Nox2 forms a heterodimer with the integral membrane protein, p22phox, and this heterodimer binds to the regulatory subunits p47phox, p67phox, p40phox and the small GTPase Rac, triggering superoxide generation. Nox-organizer protein 1 (NOXO1) and Nox-activator 1 (NOXA1), respective homologs of p47phox and p67phox, together with p22phox and Rac, activate Nox1, a non-phagocytic homolog of Nox2. NOXO1 and p22phox also regulate Nox3, whereas Nox4 requires only p22phox. In this study, we have assembled and analyzed amino acid sequences of Nox regulatory subunit orthologs from vertebrates, a urochordate, an echinoderm, a mollusc, a cnidarian, a choanoflagellate, fungi and a slime mold amoeba to investigate the evolutionary history of these subunits.
###end p 3
###begin title 4
Results
###end title 4
###begin p 5
###xml 13 17 13 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 22 26 22 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 35 40 35 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 128 148 128 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Monosiga brevicollis</italic>
###xml 262 266 262 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 271 276 271 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 353 359 353 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox- </italic>
###xml 366 370 366 370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 409 439 409 439 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Strongylocentrotus purpuratus </italic>
###xml 454 470 454 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Lottia gigantea </italic>
###xml 562 567 562 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 574 579 574 579 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 787 792 787 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 921 925 921 925 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 939 954 939 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Oryzias latipes</italic>
###xml 1045 1049 1045 1049 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 128 148 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">Monosiga brevicollis</span>
###xml 409 438 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">Strongylocentrotus purpuratus</span>
###xml 454 469 <span type="species:ncbi:225164">Lottia gigantea</span>
###xml 939 954 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">Oryzias latipes</span>
Ancestral p47phox, p67phox, and p22phox genes are broadly seen in the metazoa, except for the ecdysozoans. The choanoflagellate Monosiga brevicollis, the unicellular organism that is the closest relatives of multicellular animals, encodes early prototypes of p22phox, p47phox as well as the earliest known Nox2-like ancestor of the Nox1-3 subfamily. p67phox- and p47phox-like genes are seen in the sea urchin Strongylocentrotus purpuratus and the limpet Lottia gigantea that also possess Nox2-like co-orthologs of vertebrate Nox1-3. Duplication of primordial p47phox and p67phox genes occurred in vertebrates, with the duplicated branches evolving into NOXO1 and NOXA1. Analysis of characteristic domains of regulatory subunits suggests a novel view of the evolution of Nox: in fish, p40phox participated in regulating both Nox1 and Nox2, but after the appearance of mammals, Nox1 (but not Nox2) became independent of p40phox. In the fish Oryzias latipes, a NOXO1 ortholog retains an autoinhibitory region that is characteristic of mammalian p47phox, and this was subsequently lost from NOXO1 in later vertebrates. Detailed amino acid sequence comparisons identified both putative key residues conserved in characteristic domains and previously unidentified conserved regions. Also, candidate organizer/activator proteins in fungi and amoeba are identified and hypothetical activation models are suggested.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
Conclusion
###end title 6
###begin p 7
This is the first report to provide the comprehensive view of the molecular evolution of regulatory subunits for Nox enzymes. This approach provides clues for understanding the evolution of biochemical and physiological functions for regulatory-subunit-dependent Nox enzymes.
###end p 7
###begin title 8
Background
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 211 212 211 212 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 213 214 213 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B2">2</xref>
###xml 267 269 267 269 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ph</underline>
###xml 283 285 283 285 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ox</underline>
###xml 292 296 292 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 357 358 357 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 359 360 359 360 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B8">8</xref>
###xml 570 574 570 574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 620 625 620 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 678 682 678 682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 687 691 687 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 696 700 696 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 705 709 705 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 738 739 738 739 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 740 741 740 741 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B6">6</xref>
###xml 742 743 742 743 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 744 746 744 746 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 887 892 887 892 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox </italic>
###xml 956 957 956 957 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 958 960 958 960 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 961 963 961 963 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
Nox enzymes (reactive oxygen-generating NADPH-oxidases) diverged early in evolution into calcium-regulated Noxes (e.g., Nox5 and the Duox enzymes) and Noxes that are activated by binding to regulatory subunits [1,2]. The most extensively studied of the latter is the phagocyte NAPDH-oxidase (Phox), whose role in host defense has been documented at length [3-8]. Professional phagocytes such as neutrophils and macrophages produce large amounts of superoxide, with secondary production of other microbicidal reactive oxygen species (ROS). Superoxide is generated by the Phox, which consists of the catalytic subunit gp91phox (a.k.a. Nox2), along with the regulatory subunits p22phox, p67phox, p47phox, p40phox, and the small GTPase, Rac [3,6,9-11]. The importance of the oxidase is demonstrated by the inherited condition, chronic granulomatous disease (CGD), in which absent or mutated Phox proteins result in an inability of phagocytes to kill microbes [4,12,13].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 12 17 12 17 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 103 104 103 104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 104 107 104 107 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">558</sub>
###xml 143 144 143 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 167 171 167 171 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 176 180 176 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 189 194 189 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 284 289 284 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 308 312 308 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 334 335 334 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 336 338 336 338 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 339 341 339 341 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 342 344 342 344 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 423 424 423 424 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 425 427 425 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 777 782 777 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 789 794 789 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 848 853 848 853 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 904 909 904 909 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 910 912 910 912 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 949 953 949 953 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 957 962 957 962 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1003 1004 1003 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 1004 1007 1004 1007 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">558</sub>
###xml 1099 1104 1099 1104 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1124 1127 1124 1127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 1196 1199 1196 1199 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 1241 1245 1241 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1333 1337 1333 1337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis-</italic>
###xml 1378 1383 1378 1383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1384 1386 1384 1386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 1387 1389 1387 1389 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
###xml 1408 1413 1408 1413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1551 1553 1551 1553 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 1554 1556 1554 1556 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 1616 1621 1616 1621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1648 1653 1648 1653 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1660 1665 1660 1665 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1686 1687 1686 1687 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 1687 1690 1687 1690 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">558</sub>
###xml 1826 1831 1826 1831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1832 1834 1832 1834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 1835 1837 1835 1837 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 1872 1876 1872 1876 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1930 1932 1930 1932 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 2094 2096 2094 2096 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 2097 2099 2097 2099 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 2105 2110 2105 2110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2128 2132 2128 2132 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 2182 2187 2182 2187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2222 2226 2222 2226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2230 2235 2230 2235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2292 2294 2292 2294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 2295 2297 2295 2297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
###xml 2366 2370 2366 2370 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2392 2396 2392 2396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2496 2498 2496 2498 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 2525 2530 2525 2530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2316 2324 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
###xml 2406 2410 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
Nox2 and p22phox are integral membrane proteins that form a heterodimer referred to as flavocytochrome b558. In resting cells, flavocytochrome b558 is inactive and p47phox, p67phox, and p40phox are all present in the cytoplasm. Cell activation is accompanied by phosphorylation of p47phox and probably other Phox-regulatory subunits [3,10,14-16], and by guanine nucleotide exchange factors that convert Rac-GDP to Rac-GTP [3,17]. These events trigger assembly of these proteins at the membrane, resulting in activation of Nox2. An intricate set of protein-protein interactions facilitates the binding of the regulatory subunits to the membrane components and to each other, and these interactions are mediated by well-characterized modular interaction domains. For example, p47phox and p67phox bind via a C-terminal proline-rich region (PRR) in p47phox and a C-terminal Src homology 3 (SH3) domain in p67phox [18]. In the non-activated cell, the p47phox-p67phox complex fails to bind to flavocytochrome b558, due to an unusual autoinhibitory mechanism. In the resting cell, tandem SH3 domains in p47phox (referred to as the bis-SH3 domain) bind to an auto-inhibitory region (AIR), preventing the bis-SH3 domain from binding to the PRR of p22phox. Upon cell activation, serine residues of the AIR become phosphorylated, releasing the bis-SH3 domain so that it can now bind to p22phox [19-22]. In addition, p47phox possesses another membrane-binding region, the PX domain, which binds to the headgroups of phosphatidylinositols present in the membrane [23-25]. Together, these interactions with membrane lipids and p22phox promote the assembly of p47phox and p67phox with flavocytochrome b558. Concurrently, Rac-GTP translocates to the membrane where it interacts with the N-terminal tetratricopeptide repeat (TPR) region of p67phox [26-28]. An activation domain (AD) in p67phox, which is conformationally regulated by Rac binding [29], activates the hydride transfer from NADPH to FAD in Nox2. Subsequent electron transfer through two heme groups permits reduction of oxygen to form superoxide [30,31]. p40phox binds through its Phox/Bem 1 (PB1) domain to a partner PB1 domain in p67phox and facilitates the assembly of p67phox-p47phox at the membrane through lipid binding via its PX domain [32-34]. Although no CGD patients have been described with mutations in p40phox, neutrophils from p40phox-knockout mice exhibit CGD-like severe defects in Nox2-derived oxidant-dependent bacterial killing [35], also suggesting that p40phox is a crucial component for Nox2 function.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 27 32 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 172 173 172 173 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 174 176 174 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 332 333 332 333 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B9">9</xref>
###xml 334 336 334 336 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 529 530 525 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 693 694 689 690 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 764 769 760 765 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 817 821 813 817 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 867 869 863 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 870 872 866 868 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 873 875 869 871 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 259 265 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
The first homologue of gp91phox identified was Nox1, which is abundantly expressed in non-phagocyte cells including gastrointestinal epithelium and vascular smooth muscle [9,36]. Subsequently, additional homologues were identified, and the Nox/Duox family in humans now consists of seven members: Nox1 though Nox5, Duox1 and Duox2 [9,37]. All members of Nox/Duox family contain the six transmembrane alpha-helical heme-binding domain and an FAD domain containing an NADPH binding site, which together constitute the "Nox domain"[1]. Nox5 and Duox1/2 contain a calcium-binding EF-hand motif. The evolution of these Noxes and their calcium-binding domains were considered in the recent article [1] and are not discussed here. The remaining Noxes, Nox1-4, require p22phox for activity, and Nox1-3 all require additional Phox-like regulatory subunits, reviewed recently [10,11,37].
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 111 116 111 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 173 178 173 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 179 181 179 181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 182 184 182 184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 264 266 264 266 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 267 269 267 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 355 357 355 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 358 360 358 360 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
###xml 361 363 361 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 382 390 382 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo </italic>
###xml 522 526 522 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 630 634 630 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 706 711 706 711 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 762 770 762 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo </italic>
###xml 771 773 771 773 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 774 776 774 776 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 831 834 831 834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 902 904 902 904 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
###xml 1023 1027 1023 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1139 1143 1139 1143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1177 1181 1177 1181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1228 1233 1228 1233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1234 1236 1234 1236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 1315 1320 1315 1320 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1321 1323 1321 1323 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 1324 1326 1324 1326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 1400 1405 1400 1405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1454 1456 1454 1456 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 1457 1459 1457 1459 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 1494 1499 1494 1499 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1565 1567 1565 1567 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B52">52</xref>
###xml 1568 1570 1568 1570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54">54</xref>
###xml 1190 1195 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1252 1257 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1423 1429 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
Nox1, like gp91phox, is activated by regulatory subunits: NOXO1 (Nox-organizer protein 1) is a homologue of p47phox and NOXA1 (Nox-activator protein 1) is a homologue of p67phox [38-41]. Recent studies have also demonstrated activation of the Nox1 system by Rac1 [42-45]. NOXO1 and NOXA1 are co-expressed with Nox1 in colon epithelium and gastric mucosa [39,43,46], consistent with in vivo regulation of Nox1 by these novel subunits. Activation of Nox1 by regulatory subunits differs in two major respects compared to gp91phox. First, NOXO1 lacks the AIR and its associated regulatory phosphorylation sites that are present in p47phox. Consistent with the domain structure, NOXO1 co-localizes with Nox1/p22phox complex constitutively at/near the plasma membrane in vivo [40,41]. On the other hand, a recent study revealed that the bis-SH3 domain of NOXO1 bind to the extremely C-terminal PRR of NOXO1 [47]. Phosphorylation-independent disruption of the intramolecular interaction facilitates NOXO1 binding to the PRR of p22phox. Second, NOXA1 lacks critical basic amino acid residues in its PB1 domain that are important for binding to p40phox. NOXA1 does not interact with p40phox, making human Nox1 activity independent of p40phox [40]. Furthermore, human NOXA1 lacks the central SH3 domain that is present in p67phox [38-40], but whose function is unknown. Like Nox1, Nox3 is also regulated by p22phox and NOXO1, but in humans does not require NOXA1 [48-51]. In comparison, Nox4 requires p22phox for activity, but other known regulatory subunits are not needed [52-54].
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 262 264 262 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 448 449 448 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 481 485 481 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 527 552 527 552 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Dictyostelium discoideum </italic>
###xml 553 566 553 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum</italic>
###xml 569 571 569 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 581 586 581 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 635 649 635 649 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 721 725 721 725 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 753 755 753 755 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 763 768 763 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 878 880 878 880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 881 883 881 883 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 942 955 942 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum</italic>
###xml 999 1017 999 1017 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Epichl&#246;e festucae </italic>
###xml 1049 1051 1049 1051 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 185 191 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeasts</span>
###xml 527 551 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">Dictyostelium discoideum</span>
###xml 553 566 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 635 648 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 942 955 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 999 1016 <span type="species:ncbi:35717">Epichloe festucae</span>
Another subfamily of the Noxes is the NoxA/NoxB group, found in a slime mold amoeba and fungi. These fungal Nox genes have been identified in most ascomycetes except for hemiascomycete yeasts, and also in higher basidiomycetes and chytridiomycotes (reviewed in [55]). No Nox gene has been identified in fungi that belong to Zygomycota and Micropordia. These NoxA/NoxB genes are closely related to the subunit-regulated Noxes according to taxonomy [1]. A non-animal homologue of p67phox/NOXA1 was described in slime mold amoeba Dictyostelium discoideum (D. discoideum) [56]. The p67phox homolog (referred to here as the Dd-p67-like) of D. discoideum possesses the N-terminal TPR region and PB1 domain characteristic of p67phox, but lacks the SH3 domain [56]. A p67phox homolog Nox-regulator (NOXR) was also reported in some fungi including ascomycetes and higher basidiomycetes [55,57]. The basic motif structure of NOXR is similar to that of D. discoideum. A NOXR-deficient mutant of the ascomycete Epichloe festucae shows decreased ROS-generation [57]. Taken together, these data suggest that NOXR regulates NoxA and/or NoxB in the slime mold and fungi, although this has not been tested directly.
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 114 118 114 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 150 154 150 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 166 170 166 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 182 186 182 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 191 195 191 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 437 441 437 441 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 643 647 643 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 739 743 739 743 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
Herein, we assembled and analyzed experimentally cloned and computationally predicted amino acid sequences of the Phox-related regulatory subunits p47phox, NOXO1, p67phox, NOXA1, p40phox, p22phox, and NOXR from 10 vertebrates, one urochordate, one echinoderm, one mollusc, one cnidarian, one choanoflagellate, 13 fungi, and one slime mold amoeba. Using this large set of amino acid sequences, we report: (i) the occurrence and origin of Phox-like subunits during evolution, (ii) identification of putative key amino acid residues conserved in regulatory subunits, (iii) the description of putative new modular regions that are conserved among Phox-related regulatory subunits, (iv) the molecular evolution of characteristic domains of the Phox-related regulatory subunits, and (v) a prediction of novel fungal and amoebal Nox organizer/enhancer subunits based on sequence analysis.
###end p 14

###xml 572 577 572 577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 631 636 631 636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 673 678 673 678 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 685 690 685 690 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>

###xml 767 785 767 785 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Takifugu rubripes </italic>
###xml 786 797 786 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes</italic>
###xml 853 855 853 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58">58</xref>
###xml 935 939 935 939 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 944 948 944 948 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 953 957 953 957 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 966 971 966 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 979 981 979 981 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 999 1008 999 1008 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 1012 1023 1012 1023 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 1145 1147 1145 1147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B59">59</xref>
###xml 1166 1189 1166 1189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Tetraodon nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 1190 1205 1190 1205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis</italic>
###xml 1287 1289 1287 1289 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 1340 1342 1340 1342 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 205 210 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 211 223 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Homo sapiens</span>
###xml 225 235 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">H. sapiens</span>
###xml 238 241 <span type="species:ncbi:9615">dog</span>
###xml 278 281 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 282 299 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">Rattus norvegicus</span>
###xml 301 314 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">R. norvegicus</span>
###xml 317 322 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 323 335 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">Mus musculus</span>
###xml 337 348 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">M. musculus</span>
###xml 351 358 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">chicken</span>
###xml 359 372 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">Gallus gallus</span>
###xml 374 383 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 391 409 <span type="species:ncbi:8364">Xenopus tropicalis</span>
###xml 411 424 <span type="species:ncbi:8364">X. tropicalis</span>
###xml 440 452 <span type="species:ncbi:70862">teleost fish</span>
###xml 454 463 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">zebrafish</span>
###xml 464 475 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">Danio rerio</span>
###xml 477 485 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 488 494 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">medaka</span>
###xml 495 510 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">Oryzias latipes</span>
###xml 512 522 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 767 784 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">Takifugu rubripes</span>
###xml 786 797 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 999 1007 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 1012 1022 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 1166 1188 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">Tetraodon nigroviridis</span>
###xml 1190 1205 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
Figure 1A summarizes the occurrence of subunit-dependent-like Nox orthologs along with the Phox-like regulatory subunit orthologs in the genomes of deutrostomes, fungi, a slime mold amoeba. The tetrapods [human Homo sapiens (H. sapiens), dog Canis familliaris (C. familliaris), rat Rattus norvegicus (R. norvegicus), mouse Mus musculus (M. musculus), chicken Gallus gallus (G. gallus), frog Xenopus tropicalis (X. tropicalis)], and the two teleost fish [zebrafish Danio rerio (D. rerio), medaka Oryzias latipes (O. latipes)] have two isologs of Nox organizer proteins (p47phox and NOXO1), two isologs of Nox activator proteins (p67phox and NOXA1), and single isologs of p40phox and p22phox (Figure 1A, the sequences are provided in Additional file 1). The pufferfish Takifugu rubripes (T. rubripes), which has a compact genome size, ~400 megabase (Mb) [58], lacks NOXO1 and NOXA1 although it possesses both Nox1 and Nox2 as well as p22phox, p47phox, p67phox, and p40phox (Figure 1A), in contrast to D. rerio and O. latipes that have less compact genomes (1680-2280 Mb and 870-1100 Mb, respectively, according to the Animal Genome Size Database [59]). Interestingly, Tetraodon nigroviridis (T. nigroviridis), another species of pufferfish, which also possesses a compact genome, ~340 Mb [60], encodes a NOXO1 ortholog, but not NOXA1 (Figure 1A).
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 75 79 75 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 0 106 0 106 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Relationships between the phylogenic tree of species and the occurrence of <italic>Phox</italic>-reated regulatory subunits</bold>
###xml 109 110 109 110 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 258 268 258 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Asterisks </italic>
###xml 401 402 401 402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</italic>
###xml 527 528 518 519 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</italic>
###xml 575 576 566 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
Relationships between the phylogenic tree of species and the occurrence of Phox-reated regulatory subunits. (A) Summary of the occurrence of Nox-regulatory subunit genes in vertebrates, a urochordate, an echinoderm, fungi, and a slime mold amoeba are shown. Asterisks indicate that the gene is a co-ortholog ancestor of all members of the vertebrate Nox1-3 subgroup. Superscripted letters represent: (a), a partial amino acid sequence predicted from genomic DNA fragment (nucleotides 713622-713565 of GenBanktrade mark No. ), (b) the gene taxonomy is discussed in the text. (B) Summary of the occurrence of Nox-regulatory subunit genes within Deuterostomia. The number in the fork of each branch indicates the estimated time in millions of years (Mya, millions of years ago) since a given species diverged. A schematic phylogeny and the estimated time of occurrence of species were created from genomic information [62, 125]. Branch lengths are for illustrative purposes and are not proportional to time since divergence.
###end p 18
###begin p 19
###xml 21 40 21 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ciona intestinalis </italic>
###xml 41 56 41 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis</italic>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 109 111 109 111 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 129 159 129 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Strongylocentrotus purpuratus </italic>
###xml 160 173 160 173 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus</italic>
###xml 279 281 279 281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 284 297 284 297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus</italic>
###xml 490 491 490 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 494 510 494 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 540 545 540 545 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox-</italic>
###xml 550 555 550 555 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox-</italic>
###xml 564 568 564 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 581 583 581 583 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 638 640 638 640 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 647 661 647 661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 698 702 698 702 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 711 715 711 715 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 735 737 735 737 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 746 751 746 751 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 763 777 763 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 853 855 853 855 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 870 884 870 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 887 891 887 891 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1024 1028 1024 1028 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1051 1065 1051 1065 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 1095 1100 1095 1100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 21 39 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">Ciona intestinalis</span>
###xml 41 56 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 129 158 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">Strongylocentrotus purpuratus</span>
###xml 160 173 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 284 297 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 494 509 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 647 660 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 763 776 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 870 883 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 1051 1064 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
The earlier chordate Ciona intestinalis (C. intestinalis) possesses a Nox2 ortholog, but not Nox1 or Nox3 [1,61]. The sea urchin Strongylocentrotus purpuratus (S. purpuratus) belongs to Echinodermata, which diverged early from an ancestor common to urochordates and vertebrates [62]. S. purpuratus, possesses two Nox2 genes, Nox2A and Nox2B, and an analysis of the taxonomy Noxes demonstrates that these Nox2 genes are related to the common ancestor gene of vertebrate Nox1, Nox2 and Nox3 [1]. C. intestinalis possesses single copies of p47phox-, p67phox-, and p22phox-like genes [61], which presumably regulate its Nox2 ortholog (Figure 1A). The S. purpuratus genome possesses single copies of p47phox- and p67phox-like genes (Figure 1A). No p22phox ortholog of S. purpuratus was identified using a BLAST search of recently published genome sequences [63]. Because the S. purpuratus p47phox-like protein has a highly conserved tandem SH3 region that in other species binds to the C-terminal proline-rich region (PRR) of p22phox, it seems likely that S. purpuratus has an as-yet unidentified p22phox homologue.
###end p 19
###begin p 20
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 174 178 174 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 214 216 214 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1B</xref>
###xml 306 311 306 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 327 332 327 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 512 514 512 514 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1B</xref>
###xml 590 591 590 591 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 609 621 609 621 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 625 641 625 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 680 691 680 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 737 739 737 739 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 785 797 785 797 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 810 826 810 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 902 904 902 904 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1B</xref>
###xml 946 951 946 951 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 958 963 958 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1008 1021 1008 1021 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus</italic>
###xml 1026 1031 1026 1031 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1106 1122 1106 1122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 1125 1139 1125 1139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 1147 1149 1147 1149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1B</xref>
###xml 609 620 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 625 640 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 680 690 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 785 796 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 810 825 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 1008 1021 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 1106 1121 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 1125 1138 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
Using the estimated time of evolution of deuterostomes based on Hox gene clusters to construct a phylogenetic tree [64], we illustrate the occurrence during evolution of the Phox-related regulatory subunits(Figure 1B). The phylogenic tree suggests an evolutionary model in which duplication of both the p47phox gene and the p67phox gene occurred at a time corresponding to the appearance of vertebrates, with the NOXO1 and NOXA1 genes subsequently evolving as distinct regulatory subunits in vertebrates (Figure 1B). This appearance of NOXO1 and NOXA1 coincided with the emergence of Nox1 [1]. The pufferfish T. rubripes and T. nigroviridis are considered to have evolved from an O. latipes ancestor approximately 186 million years ago [64]. This tree suggests that NOXA1 and NOXO1 of T. rubripes and NOXA1 of T. nigroviridis have been lost during the decrease in genome sizes in these species (Figure 1B). In contrast to the co-appearance of p47phox and p67phox orthologs with the earliest Nox2 ortholog in S. purpuratus, p40phox appeared later, in vertebrates, and was not found in the genomes of either C. intestinalis or S. purpuratus (Figure 1B). The situation of the regulatory subunits of other primitive animals and a choanoflagellate is described below.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
###xml 18 22 18 22 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 62 75 62 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum</italic>
###xml 78 80 78 80 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 90 92 90 92 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 113 134 113 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Aspergillus nidulans </italic>
###xml 135 146 135 146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. nidulans</italic>
###xml 149 168 149 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Magnaporthe grisea </italic>
###xml 169 178 169 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. grisea</italic>
###xml 185 206 185 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fusarium graminearum </italic>
###xml 207 221 207 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F. graminearum</italic>
###xml 286 291 286 291 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 292 294 292 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 304 306 304 306 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 318 343 318 343 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Saccharomyces cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 344 357 344 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 435 436 435 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 437 439 437 439 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 449 451 449 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 475 495 475 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Coprinopsis cinerea </italic>
###xml 496 506 496 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. cinerea</italic>
###xml 509 526 509 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Laccaria bicolor </italic>
###xml 527 537 527 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">L. bicolor</italic>
###xml 544 560 544 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Postia placenta </italic>
###xml 561 572 561 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">P. placenta</italic>
###xml 618 620 618 620 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 762 766 762 766 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 799 804 799 804 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 812 814 812 814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 849 853 849 853 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 871 885 871 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 907 909 907 909 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 976 980 976 980 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1137 1142 1137 1142 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1155 1160 1155 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 62 75 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 113 133 <span type="species:ncbi:162425">Aspergillus nidulans</span>
###xml 135 146 <span type="species:ncbi:162425">A. nidulans</span>
###xml 149 167 <span type="species:ncbi:148305">Magnaporthe grisea</span>
###xml 169 178 <span type="species:ncbi:148305">M. grisea</span>
###xml 185 205 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">Fusarium graminearum</span>
###xml 207 221 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">F. graminearum</span>
###xml 318 342 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">Saccharomyces cerevisiae</span>
###xml 344 357 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 475 494 <span type="species:ncbi:5346">Coprinopsis cinerea</span>
###xml 496 506 <span type="species:ncbi:5346">C. cinerea</span>
###xml 509 525 <span type="species:ncbi:29883">Laccaria bicolor</span>
###xml 527 537 <span type="species:ncbi:29883">L. bicolor</span>
###xml 544 559 <span type="species:ncbi:104341">Postia placenta</span>
###xml 561 572 <span type="species:ncbi:104341">P. placenta</span>
###xml 871 884 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
A homologue of p67phox/NOXA1 occurs in the slime mold amoeba (D. discoideum) [56] (Figure 1A). Fungal genomes of Aspergillus nidulans (A. nidulans), Magnaporthe grisea (M. grisea), and Fusarium graminearum (F. graminearum), all members of Ascomycota, also possess NOXR, a homolog of p67phox [55] (Figure 1A). However, Saccharomyces cerevisiae (S. cerevisiae) that also belongs to Ascomycota does not possess any Nox or NOXR orthologs [1,55] (Figure 1A). Some basidiomycetes [Coprinopsis cinerea (C. cinerea), Laccaria bicolor (L. bicolor), and Postia placenta (P. placenta)] also possess NOXR and NoxA/B genes (Figure 1A). The situation of the regulatory subunits of other fungi is described below. Interestingly, the fungi seem to lack precise homologues of p47phox/NOXO1 or its binding partner p22phox (Figure 1A). Recently, the possibility of p22phox-like gene in the D. discoideum genome was suggested [56], but it is not clear whether the gene represents an ancestral p22phox, a later adaptation or a functionally unrelated protein. We discuss the possibilities below based on a comparison of the amino acid sequences of amoebal p22phox and other p22phox orthologs. In addition, we identified other predicted proteins encoded in fungal and amoebal genomes that may function as (a) binding partner(s) of the Nox activator proteins (described below), suggesting the early evolutionary origin not only of the activator protein, but also possibly of a rudimentary organizer subunit.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
Synteny of NOXO1 ad NOXA1 genes in vertebrates
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 82 94 82 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 98 114 98 114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 146 147 146 147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 186 198 186 198 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 499 501 499 501 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2A</xref>
###xml 560 561 560 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
###xml 651 660 651 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G. gallus</italic>
###xml 671 685 671 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">X. tropicalis </italic>
###xml 744 760 744 760 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 915 927 915 927 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 962 977 962 977 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis</italic>
###xml 1022 1024 1022 1024 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2A</xref>
###xml 1039 1048 1039 1048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 1052 1062 1052 1062 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes</italic>
###xml 1248 1250 1248 1250 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2A</xref>
###xml 1291 1302 1291 1302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 1393 1405 1393 1405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 82 93 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 98 113 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 186 197 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 420 425 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 643 650 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">chicken</span>
###xml 651 660 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 671 684 <span type="species:ncbi:8364">X. tropicalis</span>
###xml 744 759 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 915 926 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 962 977 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 1039 1047 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 1052 1062 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 1291 1301 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 1393 1404 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
An extensive BLAST search has failed to identify the NOXA1 gene in the pufferfish T. rubripes and T. nigroviridis genomes, as indicated in Figure 1. In addition to the absence of NOXA1, T. rubripes seems to have lost the NOXO1 gene. To substantiate that the NOXO1 and NOXA1 genes were indeed absent, we compared chromosomal synteny (the preserved chromosomal order of genes among organisms) of NOXO1 in vertebrates. The human NOXO1 gene is preceded by SYNGR3 and GFER genes on chromosome 16 (Figure 2A, abbreviations of gene names are shown in Additional file 2), and followed by TBL3, RPS2 and RPL3L. Synteny was preserved in mammals and the chicken G. gallus. The frog X. tropicalis lacks SYNGR3, but other markers are preserved. Among fish, T. nigroviridis conserved part of the mammalian synteny: NOXO1, TBL3, RPS2, and RPL3L and instead of SYNGR3 and GFER, C17orf39 is positioned next to NOXO1. Synteny of the T. rubripes genome was very similar to that of T. nigroviridis, although it lacks a NOXO1 ortholog (Figure 2A). Two fishes, D. rerio and O. latipes, genomes possess NOXO1 genes, but with greater variations in synteny;although TBL3 and C17orf39 were present in the same chromosome as NOXO1, other linked markers were not seen (Figure 2A). The gene markers C17orf39 and TBL3 of O. latipes are present on a separate chromosome from that of NOXO1. Thus, the synteny analysis of the T. rubripes genomes shows that the NOXO1 gene was indeed lost during evolution.
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 0 34 0 34 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Syntenies of NOXO1 and NOXA1 genes</bold>
###xml 81 82 81 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 95 96 95 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 294 295 294 295 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S2">2</xref>
Syntenies of NOXO1 and NOXA1 genes. Syntenies of the indicated vertebrate NOXO1 (A) and NOXA1 (B) genes are shown. Genes are aligned in columns to illustrate orthology. Chromosome (Chr) or scaffold (Sc) number is indicated on the right. Abbreviations of gene names are shown in Additional file 2.
###end p 24
###begin p 25
###xml 73 83 73 83 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">H. sapiens</italic>
###xml 85 99 85 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. familliaris</italic>
###xml 101 124 101 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. musculus, G. gallus </italic>
###xml 132 134 132 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2B</xref>
###xml 174 188 174 188 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R. norvegicus </italic>
###xml 269 271 269 271 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2B</xref>
###xml 291 304 291 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">X. tropicalis</italic>
###xml 513 524 513 524 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 528 537 528 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 625 627 625 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2B</xref>
###xml 630 646 630 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 726 738 726 738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 760 768 760 768 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio</italic>
###xml 73 83 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">H. sapiens</span>
###xml 101 112 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">M. musculus</span>
###xml 114 123 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 174 187 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">R. norvegicus</span>
###xml 291 304 <span type="species:ncbi:8364">X. tropicalis</span>
###xml 513 523 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 528 536 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 630 645 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 726 737 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 760 768 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
The synteny of genetic markers surrounding NOXA1 was highly conserved in H. sapiens, C. familliaris, M. musculus, G. gallus (Figure 2B). Both NOXA1 and the linked markers of R. norvegicus were present in chromosome 3, with a long insert between NOXA1and ENTPD8 (Figure 2B). In the genome of X. tropicalis, synteny was more varied in that NOXA1 and ENTPD8 were present in the same scaffold, but other markers were not seen. Synteny of fish NOXA1 was preserved among the class but different from other vertebrates. O. latipes and D. rerio NOXA1 genes are preceded by MAN1B1 and DPP7 on chromosome 9 and 5, respectively (Figure 2B). T. nigroviridis possesses two markers MAN1B1 and DPP7, but lacks the NOXA1 ortholog. Synteny of T. rubripes is similar to that of D. rerio, but a NOXA1 ortholog is absent. Thus, the synteny of NOXA1 had considerable variation, and this analysis indicates that NOXA1 orthologs were lost during the evolution of the two pufferfish genomes.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 67 71 67 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
Identification of putative critical amino acids conserved among p47phox/NOXO1 orthologs
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 20 25 20 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 168 169 168 169 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 183 185 183 185 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2 </sub>
###xml 201 203 201 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 204 206 204 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 321 322 321 322 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 401 403 401 403 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2 </sub>
###xml 404 406 404 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 407 409 407 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B65">65</xref>
###xml 424 427 424 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 459 463 459 463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 505 507 505 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3A</xref>
###xml 644 646 644 646 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3A</xref>
###xml 730 733 730 733 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 764 766 764 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3A</xref>
###xml 854 857 854 857 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 879 884 879 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 917 919 917 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3A</xref>
###xml 1021 1026 1021 1026 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1027 1029 1027 1029 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 1030 1032 1030 1032 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B66">66</xref>
###xml 1033 1035 1033 1035 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 226 231 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 870 875 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1004 1009 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
The PX domain of p47phox binds with highest affinity to phosphatidylinositol 3,4-bisphosphate [PtdIns(3,4)P2], and with lower but significant affinity to PtdIns(3,4,5)P3, PtdIns(3,5)P2 and PtdIns(3)P [23-25]. The PX domain of human NOXO1 shows a different lipid binding specificity, with highest affinity for PtdIns(3,5)P2, PtdIns(5)P, and PtdIns(4)P and lower affinity for PtdIns(3)P and PtdIns(3,4)P2 [41,65]. Both PX and bis-SH3 domains are seen in all p47phox/NOXO1 orthologs of deuterostomes (Figure 3A). Comparison of the sequences of the organizer proteins allowed identification of amino acid residues that are highly conserved (Figure 3A). Eleven highly conserved residues were identified in the PX domain, and 22 in the bis-SH3 domains (arrows in Figure 3A). Arg-42, Pro-73, and Arg-90 of the PX-domain and Trp-193, Phe-209, and Trp-263 of the bis-SH3 domain (human-p47phox numbering, black boxes in Figure 3A) were previously shown by mutational analyses to be essential for the activation of human Nox2 by p47phox [24,66-68].
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 0 69 0 69 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Identification of highly conserved residues of Nox organizer proteins</bold>
###xml 134 144 134 144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">H. sapiens</italic>
###xml 150 164 150 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. familliaris</italic>
###xml 170 183 170 183 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R. norvegicus</italic>
###xml 189 200 189 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. musculus</italic>
###xml 206 215 206 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G. gallus</italic>
###xml 221 234 221 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">X. tropicalis</italic>

###xml 345 346 345 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 408 413 408 413 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox </italic>

###xml 912 913 912 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 992 995 992 995 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 1010 1011 1010 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
