###xml 1137 1142 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1596 1601 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Identification of highly conserved residues of Nox organizer proteins. Species names were abbreviated as follows: v-, vertebrate; Hs, H. sapiens; Cf, C. familliaris; Rn, R. norvegicus; Mm, M. musculus; Gg, G. gallus; Xt, X. tropicalis, Dr, D. rerio; Tr, T. rubripes; Tn, T. nigroviridis; Ol, O. latipes; Ci, C. intestinalis; Sp, S. purpuratus. (A) Schematic domain structures of Nox organizer are shown; PX, Phox homology; SH3, the Src homology 3; AIR, autoinhibitory region; PRR, proline-rich region; C-tail, C-terminal tail region. Orthologs that possess these domains are shown below the domains. Amino acid residues indicate conserved amino acids in all Nox-organizers. Residue numbers correspond to those of the human p47phox protein sequence. Letters in solid boxes indicate the residues that have been previously proven by mutational analyses to be essential for the human Nox2 activation [24, 68, 126]. (B) Molecular taxonomy was created comparing by the sequence spanning the PX and bis-SH3 domains. (C) Alignment of amino acid sequences of the AIR. Letters in solid boxes indicate residues previously shown to be essential for human Nox2 activation, determined by mutational analyses [20] and also key residues responsible for interactions with the bis-SH3 domain, shown by X-ray crystallography [21]. (D) Alignment of amino acid sequences of the PRR and C-tail regions. Letters in solid boxes indicate the residues that have been shown by mutational analyses to be important for binding to p67phox [18, 72]. An arrow head indicates a residue corresponding to a phosphorylation site of human p47phox [19].
###end p 28
###begin p 29
###xml 17 20 17 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 57 62 57 62 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 101 115 101 115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 119 134 119 134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis</italic>
###xml 263 268 263 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 319 321 319 321 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 404 406 404 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 407 409 407 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 479 483 479 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 501 515 501 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 519 535 519 535 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 557 559 557 559 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 657 662 657 662 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 679 681 679 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 711 713 711 713 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 101 114 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 119 134 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 501 514 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 519 534 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
While the PX and bis-SH3 domains are shared among all p47phox and NOXO1 orthologs including those of S. purpuratus and C. intestinalis, the molecular taxonomy of the regions (excluding the variable C-terminal regulator docking regions) reveals that vertebrate p47phox and NOXO1 families form distinct subgroups (Figure 3B), likely accounting, for example, for differences in lipid binding specificities [24,41]. The phylogenic tree supports an evolutionary model in which the p47phox-like proteins of S. purpuratus and C. intestinalis (#21 and 20 of Figure 3B, respectively) branch from a root that is closely related to the primordial ancestors of both p47phox (#1-10 of Figure 3B) and NOXO1 (#11-19 of Figure 3B).
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 15 20 15 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 73 77 73 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 88 93 88 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 103 106 103 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 139 141 139 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 142 144 142 144 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 145 147 145 147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B69">69</xref>
###xml 192 194 192 194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 195 197 195 197 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 419 423 419 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 469 474 469 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 506 508 506 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3C</xref>
###xml 525 541 525 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 545 559 545 559 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 562 567 562 567 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 614 616 614 616 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3C</xref>
###xml 619 633 619 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 747 752 747 752 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 942 952 942 952 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes</italic>
###xml 1001 1006 1001 1006 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1034 1036 1034 1036 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3C</xref>
###xml 1183 1187 1183 1187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1237 1248 1237 1248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 79 84 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 179 184 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 410 415 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 525 540 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 545 558 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 619 632 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 929 941 <span type="species:ncbi:70862">teleost fish</span>
###xml 942 952 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 1237 1247 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
To maintain p47phox strictly in an inactive state that cannot bind to p22phox, human p47phox masks its bis-SH3 domain with the AIR region [21,68,69], and this region is absent in human NOXO1 [38-41]. Therefore Nox2 activity is considered more tightly controlled than Nox1 activity. Most residues essential for the function of the AIR (e.g., Pro-299, Pro-300, Arg-301, Arg-302, Ser-303, Ser- 304 and Ser-328 of human p47phox), are well conserved among all vertebrate p47phox proteins (black boxes of Figure 3C). Interestingly C. intestinalis and S. purpuratus p47phox proteins possessed the AIR-like region (Figure 3C). S. purpuratus possesses two Nox2-like proteins Nox2A and 2B that are co-orthologs of vertebrate Noxes 1-3; the presence of a p47phox ortholog harboring the AIR suggests that this primitive Nox system functions analogously to the mammalian Nox2 system. All NOXO1 orthologs lack the AIR, with one exception, the teleost fish O. latipes, which retains the predicted AIR in both the p47phox and the NOXO1 genes (Figure 3C). Thus, this analysis supports an evolutionary model in which the NOXO1 "AIR-independent" Nox1 and Nox3 activation systems originated from the p47phox-like "AIR-dependent" Nox2 regulatory system. The O. latipes NOXO1, which contains the AIR, represents an evolutionary remnant reflecting the transition from AIR-dependence to -independence.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
###xml 35 40 35 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 47 52 47 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 117 122 117 122 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 158 163 158 163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 164 166 164 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 167 169 167 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B70">70</xref>
###xml 170 172 170 172 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B72">72</xref>
###xml 229 234 229 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 241 246 241 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 305 307 305 307 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3A</xref>
###xml 341 346 341 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 491 493 491 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 536 541 536 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 638 643 638 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 772 777 772 777 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 796 798 796 798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 944 946 944 946 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 1001 1003 1001 1003 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 1084 1089 1084 1089 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1114 1119 1114 1119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1120 1122 1120 1122 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 1246 1251 1246 1251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1297 1299 1297 1299 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 1347 1352 1347 1352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1366 1371 1366 1371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1383 1385 1383 1385 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 1386 1388 1386 1388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B72">72</xref>
###xml 1490 1495 1490 1495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1569 1574 1569 1574 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1611 1616 1611 1616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1634 1636 1634 1636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 1687 1692 1687 1692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1846 1851 1846 1851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1878 1880 1878 1880 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 1981 1986 1981 1986 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1998 2000 1998 2000 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B72">72</xref>
###xml 2085 2090 2085 2090 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2094 2103 2094 2103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G. gallus</italic>
###xml 2105 2114 2105 2114 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 2118 2129 2118 2129 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 2149 2163 2149 2163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">an arrow head </italic>
###xml 2173 2175 2173 2175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 2252 2257 2252 2257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 26 31 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 629 634 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 763 768 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1237 1242 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1560 1565 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1837 1842 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 2094 2103 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 2105 2113 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 2118 2128 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
The heterodimerization of human p47phox and p67phox is dependent on the interaction between the C-terminal PRR of p47phox and the C-terminal SH3 domain of p67phox [40,70-72]. Both of these regions were conserved in vertebrate p47phox and p67phox orthologs, but not in orthologs of lower organisms (Figure 3A). The alignment of vertebrate p47phox and NOXO1 amino acid sequences demonstrates that in addition to the PRR, the C-terminal region immediately following the PRR ("C-tail" in Figure 3D) was also highly conserved. The PRR of p47phox isologs possesses four strictly conserved residues (Pro-363, Pro-366, Arg-368, Pro-369; human-p47phox numbering), and the C-tail region had an additional four identical amino acids (Ile-374, Arg-377, Cys-378, and Thr-382; human-p47phox numbering) (Figure 3D). Consistent with these identities, the essential binding roles of three residues (Pro-363, Pro-366, Arg-368, indicated by black boxes of Figure 3D) were previously demonstrated by mutational analyses [18]. The C-tail region is thought to enhance the interaction between the PRR of p47phox and the SH3 domain of p67phox [18], since simultaneous mutation of six of these residues (Leu-373, Ile-374, Arg-377, Thr-382, Lys-383, and Lys-385; human-p47phox numbering, indicated by black boxes of Figure 3D) significantly decreased the binding of the p47phox PRR to the p67phox SH3 domain [18,72]. Four of these residues (Ile-374, Arg-377, Thr-382, and Lys-383) are highly conserved among both p47phox and NOXO1 proteins, but two other residues (Leu-373 and Lys-385; human-p47phox numbering) were conserved only in p47phox orthologs (Figure 3D). This suggests that the binding affinities of p47phox and NOXO1 toward their respective activator protein SH3 domains may differ due to differences in these residues. Ser-379 in the C-tail region of human p47phox is a phosphorylation site [19]; the phosphorylation of which negatively regulates binding of the PRR and C-tail regions to the p67phox SH3 domain [72]. The threonine or serine residue is conserved at the position in all vertebrate p47phox and G. gallus, D. rerio and O. latipes NOXO1 (indicated by an arrow head in Figure 3D), indicating that NOXO1 proteins of these species retain this feature of p47phox which is subsequently lost in higher vertebrate NOXO1.
###end p 31
###begin title 32
###xml 0 12 0 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 0 11 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
T. rubripes C17orf39 ortholog as a candidate NOXO1-like protein
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 48 60 48 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 87 89 87 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2A</xref>
###xml 218 220 218 220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B73">73</xref>
###xml 269 278 269 278 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 282 298 282 298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. nigroviridis </italic>
###xml 314 316 314 316 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">2A</xref>
###xml 420 422 420 422 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4B</xref>
###xml 514 526 514 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 652 655 652 655 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 698 700 698 700 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4A</xref>
###xml 719 731 719 731 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 788 791 788 791 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 810 815 810 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 833 835 833 835 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4C</xref>
###xml 912 914 912 914 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4D</xref>
###xml 985 990 985 990 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1015 1027 1015 1027 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 1044 1046 1044 1046 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F4">4D</xref>
###xml 1195 1207 1195 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 48 59 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 269 277 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 282 297 <span type="species:ncbi:99883">T. nigroviridis</span>
###xml 514 525 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 719 730 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 976 981 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1015 1026 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
###xml 1195 1206 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
The NOXO1 gene seems to have been lost from the T. rubripes genome, as shown in Figure 2A. On the other hand, orthologs of chromosome 17 open reading frame 39 (C17orf39) gene predicted by the ensembl transcript model [73] are present adjacent to the NOXO1 genes in the D. rerio and T. nigroviridis genomes (Figure 2A). Amino acid sequences of these C17orf39 orthologs showed conserved PRR and polybasic regions (Figure. 4B, respectively, indicated by black boxes). In addition to the PRR and polybasic region, the T. rubripes C17orf39 ortholog has an extended region that encodes domains analogous to the C-terminal regions of NOXO1; these contain the bis-SH3 domain, PRR and C-tail region (Figure 4A). The sequence of T. rubripes C17orf39 possesses the 22 residues that are conserved in bis-SH3 domains of p47phox and NOXO1 (Figure 4C) and the eight key residues conserved in the PRR and C-tail regions (Figure 4D). A phosphorylation site corresponding to Ser-379 residue of human p47phox is also conserved in the T. rubripes C17orf39 (Figure 4D). Although the function of C17orf39 has not been established in any species, its NOXO1-like domain structure suggests that the C17orf39 ortholog of T. rubripes may function in place of the authentic NOXO1.
###end p 33

###begin title 35
###xml 67 71 67 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
Identification of putative critical amino acids conserved among p67phox/NOXA1 orthologs
###end title 35
###begin p 36
###xml 173 175 173 175 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5A</xref>
###xml 265 270 265 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 333 335 333 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 345 347 345 347 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5A</xref>
###xml 413 418 413 418 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 419 421 419 421 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 444 449 444 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 558 560 558 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 561 563 561 563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 586 591 586 591 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 623 634 623 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. nidulans</italic>
###xml 678 680 678 680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 704 714 704 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. grisea </italic>
###xml 718 732 718 732 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F. graminearum</italic>
###xml 821 823 821 823 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 866 880 866 880 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 883 887 883 887 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 908 912 908 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1036 1038 1036 1038 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 1209 1211 1209 1211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 1212 1214 1212 1214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 1215 1217 1215 1217 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 1218 1220 1218 1220 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B74">74</xref>
###xml 1308 1312 1308 1312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1374 1378 1374 1378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1465 1467 1465 1467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5B</xref>
###xml 1522 1526 1522 1526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1563 1577 1563 1577 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 1581 1597 1581 1597 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 1622 1624 1622 1624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5B</xref>
###xml 1666 1671 1666 1671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1679 1681 1679 1681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 1697 1698 1697 1698 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 1778 1783 1778 1783 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1790 1795 1790 1795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1981 1985 1981 1985 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2005 2007 2005 2007 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5B</xref>
###xml 256 261 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 435 440 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 490 495 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 623 634 <span type="species:ncbi:162425">A. nidulans</span>
###xml 704 713 <span type="species:ncbi:148305">M. grisea</span>
###xml 718 732 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">F. graminearum</span>
###xml 866 879 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 1299 1304 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1563 1576 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 1581 1596 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
Alignment of the amino acid sequences of the 24 Nox-activator proteins (including amoebal and fungal isologs) identified 13 conserved amino acids in the TPR domains (Figure 5A). This includes two residues that have been identified as essential for binding human p67phox to Rac, as determined by the crystal structure of the complex [21] (Figure 5A, filled boxes). The AD was first identified by mutagenesis of p67phox [30]. Val-204 of human p67phox and the corresponding residue Val-205 of human NOXA1 are crucial for respective activation of Nox2 and Nox1 [30,41]. All orthologs of p67phox and NOXA1, and one fungal NOXR (A. nidulans-NOXR) conserve this valine residue (Figure 5C). The two fungal NOXR (M. grisea and F. graminearum) retained the hydrophobic amino acid leucine instead of valine at this position (Figure 5C). Similarly, the second AD-like region of S. purpuratus p67phox-like protein (Sp-p67phox-C) conserved an isoleucine residue at this position. In contrast, Dd-p67-like protein lacked a typical AD sequence (Figure 5C). The N-terminal region containing the TPR and AD can be considered as the "Nox-activating region", a module that cooperates with Rac to activate Nox enzymatic activity [11,29-31,74]. Taxonomy of the "Nox-activating region" (corresponding to residues 1-212 of human p67phox) reveals distinct subgroups corresponding to NOXA1 and to p67phox, and shows that the NOXR proteins of fungi also represent a distinct subgroup (Figure 5B). A fourth rather diverse subgroup is comprised of p67phox-like proteins that include those of S. purpuratus and C. intestinalis (numbers 19-21 in Figure 5B). Taken together with the taxonomy of p47phox (Figure 3B) and of Noxes [1], these data support an evolutionary model in which duplication of both the p67phox and p47phox genes occurred in vertebrates at a time corresponding to the appearance of Nox1. In contrast to fungal NOXR, Dd-p67-like protein appeared to branch from a root shared with sea urchin-p67phox-like genes (Figure 5B); however, the bootstrap value was only 35% raising uncertainty as to which subgroup the amoebal p67-like protein belongs. Nevertheless, amoebal p67-like protein is clearly distinct from the NOXR group.
###end p 36

###begin p 38
###xml 185 190 185 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 198 200 198 200 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5A</xref>
###xml 248 253 248 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 333 335 333 335 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5A</xref>
###xml 356 357 356 357 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S3">3</xref>
###xml 439 441 439 441 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">AD</underline>
###xml 442 443 442 443 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S</underline>
###xml 446 447 446 447 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">I</underline>
###xml 458 459 458 459 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S</underline>
###xml 512 517 512 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 637 639 637 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5D</xref>
###xml 690 694 690 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 768 773 768 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 820 822 820 822 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5D</xref>
###xml 1031 1036 1031 1036 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1087 1089 1087 1089 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 1090 1092 1090 1092 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B75">75</xref>
###xml 681 686 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
In contrast to the C-terminal SH3 domain (SH3-B) of activator proteins which is seen in all vertebrate activator proteins, the central SH3 domain (SH3-A) was seen only in vertebrate p67phox (Figure 5A). Comparison of sequences of all vertebrate p67phox orthologs identified 31 highly conserved amino acids in this SH3 domain (Figure 5A and Additional file 3). In addition, a region between AD and SH3-A (termed here the ADSIS region for " AD-SH3 Intervening Sequence") was strictly conserved among vertebrate p67phox isologs, but was not seen in others, such as NOXA1 and NOXR. A consensus sequence was identified in this region (Figure 5D). A PRR-like region (residues 227-231 of human p67phox) was seen in ADSIS region, but it does not conserve in all vertebrate p67phox isologs based on the deduced sequences (Figure 5D). The role of the putative region is currently unknown, but may involve a function related to SH3-A because it coincides with the presence of SH3-A. Despite the high conservation of SH3-A among vertebrate p67phox orthologs, the role of this domain is not defined [10,75].
###end p 38
###begin p 39
###xml 48 52 48 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 134 150 134 150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 154 168 154 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 171 175 171 175 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>

###xml 468 473 468 473 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 517 521 517 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>

###xml 945 950 945 950 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 988 993 988 993 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">both </italic>
###xml 1105 1109 1105 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1144 1160 1144 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 1164 1178 1164 1178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 1181 1185 1181 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1237 1242 1237 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1277 1279 1277 1279 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1B</xref>
###xml 134 149 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 154 167 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 339 344 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 459 464 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 558 565 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">chicken</span>
###xml 567 576 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 588 596 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 601 611 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 761 768 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">chicken</span>
###xml 819 832 <span type="species:ncbi:8364">X. tropicalis</span>
###xml 1144 1159 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 1164 1177 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
The PB1 domain was present in all vertebrate p67phox, in vertebrate NOXA1 and in fungal NOXR and amoebal p67-like protein, but not in C. intestinalis and S. purpuratus p67phox-like proteins (Figure 5A). The crystal structure of the heterodimer between the PB1 domains of p67phox and p40phox domain demonstrated that Lys-355 and Lys-382 in human p67phox are essential to bind the PB1 domain of p40phox [32,76]. Residues corresponding to Lys-355 and Lys-382 of human p67phox are conserved not only in the vertebrate p67phox, but also in the NOXA1 orthologs of chicken (G. gallus) and fish (D. rerio and O. latipes) (Figure 5E). This suggests that in addition to its well-described role in activating Nox2, p40phox probably also participates in activating Nox1 in chicken and fish (Figure 5E). On the other hand, NOXA1 of X. tropicalis has lost both of these p40phox-interacting residues. Thus, these data support an evolutionary model in which p40phox originally participated in regulating both Nox1 and Nox2 in vertebrates, but after the appearance of mammals, Nox1 (but not Nox2) became independent of p40phox. The lack of a PB1 domain in both C. intestinalis and S. purpuratus p67phox-like proteins is consistent with the absence of p40phox orthologs in these species (Figure 1B).
###end p 39
###begin p 40
###xml 163 168 163 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 206 209 206 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e.g</italic>
###xml 228 233 228 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 247 258 247 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">gray boxes </italic>
###xml 268 270 268 270 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 343 363 343 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G. gallus, D. rerio </italic>
###xml 367 378 367 378 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 386 388 386 388 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 435 437 435 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5E</xref>
###xml 474 478 474 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 501 503 501 503 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 568 582 568 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 585 589 585 589 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 705 707 705 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5E</xref>
###xml 772 774 772 774 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 939 944 939 944 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1042 1047 1042 1047 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1105 1107 1105 1107 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5F</xref>
###xml 1240 1245 1240 1245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1252 1257 1252 1257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1366 1368 1366 1368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3D</xref>
###xml 1492 1497 1492 1497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 343 352 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 354 362 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 367 377 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 568 581 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 930 935 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
The analysis of PB1 domain sequences in Nox activators also suggests an unexpected relationship between the AD and the PB1 domain. AD regions of all vertebrate p67phox contain a positively charged residue, e.g., Lys-196 of h-p67phox (indicated by gray boxes in Figure 5C). This basic residue is also completely conserved in NOXA1 orthologs of G. gallus, D. rerio and O. latipes (Figure 5C), which retain functional PB1 domains (Figure 5E), but not in the other NOXA1 and p67phox-like proteins (Figure 5C) (with the single exception of the C-terminal AD-like region of S. purpuratus p67phox-like protein). Interestingly, the fungal NOXR, which possess these key basic residues in their PB1 domains (Figure 5E), also conserves this basic residue in their AD regions (Figure 5C). Thus, the presence of a functional PB1 domain correlates strongly with the presence of a positively charged residue corresponding to position 196 in the human p67phox sequence, and may point to the functional cooperation of these two regions, e.g. in binding to p40phox or other functionally analogous proteins in fungi (Figure 5F). Alternatively, the positively charged residue in AD region might be related to the tail-to-tail interaction between vertebrate p47phox and p67phox (and NOXO1-NOXA1 of early vertebrates) because a sequence analysis of Nox organizers that is shown in Figure 3D suggests that the conserved residue also co-occurs with the phosphorylation site in the C-tail region of all vertebrate p47phox and early vertebrate NOXO1. Thus, co-appearance and co-disappearance of evolutionarily conserved residue provides a hint to find an unknown relationship between regulatory-subunits.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 36 41 36 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 68 82 68 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 85 89 85 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 111 113 111 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5A</xref>
###xml 208 210 208 210 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5A</xref>
###xml 270 274 270 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 394 396 394 396 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 68 81 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 261 266 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
SH3-B was seen in all vertebrate p67phox and NOXA1 orthologs and in S. purpuratus p67phox-like protein (Figure 5A). Among these orthologs, seven conserved amino acid residues in SH3-B were identified (Figure 5A), and the residues include a tryptophan (Trp-494; human p67phox- numbering) that was previously shown to be crucial for interaction with the C-terminal PRR of Nox organizer proteins [40].
###end p 41
###begin title 42
###xml 67 72 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
Identification of putative critical amino acids conserved among p40phox orthologs
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 13 18 13 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 70 72 70 72 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 73 75 73 75 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 76 78 76 78 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B77">77</xref>
###xml 79 81 79 81 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B78">78</xref>
###xml 87 92 87 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 137 139 137 139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1B</xref>
###xml 196 200 196 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 295 297 295 297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5E</xref>
###xml 346 351 346 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 400 405 400 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 509 514 509 514 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 532 534 532 534 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6A</xref>
###xml 568 573 568 573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 661 662 661 662 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S3">3</xref>
###xml 725 730 725 730 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 811 813 811 813 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 814 816 814 816 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 817 819 817 819 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B79">79</xref>
###xml 820 822 820 822 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B80">80</xref>
###xml 891 893 891 893 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6B</xref>
###xml 983 988 983 988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1033 1035 1033 1035 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B81">81</xref>
###xml 1330 1335 1330 1335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1347 1349 1347 1349 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B82">82</xref>
###xml 1428 1433 1428 1433 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1463 1464 1463 1464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S3">3</xref>
###xml 1772 1786 1772 1786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">X. tropicalis </italic>
###xml 1789 1794 1789 1794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1831 1836 1831 1836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1857 1858 1857 1858 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S3">3</xref>
###xml 716 721 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1321 1326 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1599 1604 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1772 1785 <span type="species:ncbi:8364">X. tropicalis</span>
###xml 1824 1827 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
Mammalian p40phox is considered to be an enhancer of Nox2 activation [33,35,77,78]. p40phox orthologs emerged in vertebrates (see Figure 1B) coincident with the appearance of the PB1 domain of p67phox-like proteins. Fungal NOXR and amoebal p67-like proteins also possess the PB1 domains (Figure 5E), but their genomes do not encode a distinct p40phox ortholog. The protein sequences of vertebrate p40phox orthologs are highly conserved; the canonical PX, SH3, and PB1 domains are all seen among vertebrate p40phox orthologs (Figure 6A). Alignment of ten vertebrate p40phox orthologs showed 48 conserved amino acid residues in the PX domain (see Additional file 3), including Phe-35, Arg-57, Tyr-59, Leu-65, Arg-105 (human p40phox numbering) that have been demonstrated to be essential for phospholipid-binding [23,24,79,80]. Phylogenic analysis using the trimmed PX domain sequences (Figure 6B) does not reveal obvious sub-families. Recently a novel intramolecular interaction in p40phox between the PX and PB1 domains was reported [81]. The interface between the PX and PB1 domains consists of a hydrophobic pocket by Phe-35 of the PX domain and Val-257, Pro-265, Leu-273 and Phe-320 of the PB1 domain and ionic interactions between His-38, Arg-58, and Arg-60 of the PX domain and Glu-259 and Asp-269 of the PB1 domain (human p40phox numbering) [82]. The residue corresponding to the Leu-273 is much varied among vertebrate p40phox proteins (see Additional file 3), suggesting that the residue is less crucial than that previously proposed if the interaction is important in other vertebrates than human. The residue to His-38 is often replaced by tyrosine. The majority of other residues are conserved, but there are some exceptions: residues corresponding to Arg-60 in X. tropicalis p40phox and to Glu-259 and Asp-269 in rat p40phox (see Additional file 3).
###end p 43
###begin p 44
###xml 50 54 50 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 0 54 0 54 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Identification of highly conserved residues of p40<italic>phox</italic></bold>
###xml 57 58 57 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 88 93 88 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 226 237 226 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">gray boxes </italic>
###xml 335 347 335 347 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">solid boxes </italic>
###xml 508 513 508 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 549 550 549 550 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 499 504 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Identification of highly conserved residues of p40phox. (A) A schematic structure of p40phox domains is shown; proline-basic region, P-basic. Abbreviations of domain names are described in legends to other Figures. Letters in gray boxes indicate highly conserved proline and basic amino acid residues in the P-basic region. Letters in solid boxes indicate key acidic residues of OPCA motif that have been demonstrated by X-ray crystallographic structure [32]. K355 and K382 indicate two residues of human p67phox that interact with the OPCA motif. (B) Molecular taxonomy was generated by the alignment of amino acid sequences of PX domain. Species name abbreviations are given in Figure 3.
###end p 44
###begin p 45
###xml 62 67 62 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 89 91 89 91 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 168 169 168 169 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S3">3</xref>
###xml 378 380 378 380 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6A</xref>
###xml 454 459 454 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 470 472 470 472 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
###xml 473 475 473 475 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B80">80</xref>
###xml 625 630 625 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 631 633 631 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B81">81</xref>
###xml 634 636 634 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B82">82</xref>
###xml 761 763 761 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B82">82</xref>
###xml 840 845 840 845 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 949 954 949 954 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1040 1044 1040 1044 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1081 1085 1081 1085 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1175 1177 1175 1177 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 1243 1248 1243 1248 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1266 1268 1266 1268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6A</xref>
###xml 1031 1036 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1072 1077 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
To the best of our knowledge, a role for the SH3 domain of p40phox has not been defined [10]. Eighteen amino acids are conserved in the SH3 domain (see Additional file 3). Between the PX and SH3 domains, we identified a new conserved region of 15 amino acids that is rich in proline, arginine and lysine, and is therefore designated the "proline-basic (P-basic) domain" (Figure 6A). This putative region is not essential for PtdIns(3)P-binding by the p40phox PX domain [25,80]. An intramolecular interaction between the PX and PB1 domains seem not to be related to P-basic region according to the structure of full length p40phox [81,82]. The structural analysis demonstrates that P-basic region forms a separate motif and is situated closely to the PX domain [82], indicating that it might support the cell membrane-binding function of p40phox together with the PX-domain. Alternatively, the P-basic region might interact with the SH3 domain of p40phox in a manner similar to the interaction between the AIR and the tandem SH3 of human p47phox. Interestingly, Thr-154 of human p40phox, located in the center of P-basic region, has been identified as a phosphorylation site [16], and this residue is entirely conserved among all vertebrate p40phox orthologs (Figure 6A).
###end p 45
###begin p 46
###xml 27 32 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 78 79 78 79 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O</underline>
###xml 82 84 82 84 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">PC</underline>
###xml 85 86 85 86 <underline xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</underline>
###xml 223 228 223 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 240 242 240 242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 319 324 319 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 447 462 447 462 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. familliaris </italic>
###xml 465 470 465 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 510 515 510 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 523 525 523 525 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6A</xref>
###xml 18 23 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 310 315 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 501 506 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
The PB1 domain of human p40phox harbors acidic amino acids forming the "OPCA (OPR/PC/AID) motif". An OPCA motif contains four distinctive acidic residues that are essential for binding to conserved basic residues in the p67phox PB1 domain [32]. The four acidic residues, Asp-289, Glu-291, Asp-293 and Asp-302 (human p40phox numbering) are conserved in all orthologs with the exception of a glutamine rather than a glutamic acid in the position of C. familliaris p40phox that corresponds to Glu-291 of human p40phox (Figure 6A).
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 67 72 67 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
Identification of putative critical amino acids conserved among p22phox orthologs
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 9 14 9 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 60 62 60 62 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B83">83</xref>
###xml 145 147 145 147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 148 150 148 150 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 167 172 167 172 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 258 259 258 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B3">3</xref>
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 306 311 306 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 329 331 329 331 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7A</xref>
###xml 379 380 379 380 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S4">4</xref>
###xml 434 437 434 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 536 541 536 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 559 561 559 561 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7A</xref>
###xml 754 756 754 756 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7B</xref>
###xml 840 842 840 842 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7A</xref>
###xml 1071 1073 1071 1073 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B84">84</xref>
###xml 1074 1076 1074 1076 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B86">86</xref>
###xml 1153 1158 1153 1158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1434 1437 1434 1437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e.g</italic>
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
###xml 1224 1229 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Human p22phox contains two predicted transmembrane regions [83] and forms a stabilizing heterocomplex with Nox2 as well as Nox1, Nox3, and Nox4 [51-53]. The PRR of p22phox is the only motif in this protein whose role in Nox activation has been demonstrated [3,10]. The PRR is highly conserved among all p22phox orthologs (Figure 7A, the sequences are provided in Additional file 4), consistent with its role as a docking site for the bis-SH3 domain of organizer proteins. In addition, a total of 38 amino acids were identical in all p22phox sequences (Figure 7A), suggesting important additional functions, particularly for the N-terminal regions preceding TM1. Within these conserved residues, we identified a region rich in arginine and lysine (Figure 7B), and is therefore designated the polybasic region (indicated as "basic" in Figure 7A). A short sequence containing multiple basic amino acid residues has been proposed to contribute to recruitment of proteins to membrane sub-regions and to function in receptor-internalization via interaction with phospholipids [84-86]. According to our preliminary data, mutation in the polybasic region of p22phox did not affect extracellular ROS production from Nox2-transfected human embryonic kidney 293 cells (T. Kawahara and J. D. Lambeth, unpublished observations). This implies that the putative conserved region might function in a role unrelated to the enzymatic activity of Nox2, e.g. in phagocytosis or receptor-mediated endocytosis.
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 50 54 50 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 0 54 0 54 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Identification of highly conserved residues of p22<italic>phox</italic></bold>
###xml 57 58 57 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 95 100 95 100 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 148 151 148 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">st </sup>
###xml 156 159 156 159 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nd </sup>
###xml 362 367 362 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 434 438 434 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 483 487 483 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(B) </italic>
###xml 499 503 499 503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">(C) </italic>
###xml 525 537 525 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">solid boxes </italic>
###xml 638 643 638 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 696 697 696 697 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 797 801 797 801 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 425 430 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 664 669 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Identification of highly conserved residues of p22phox. (A) Schematic domains structures of p22phox are shown; TM1 and TM2 represent the predicted 1st and 2nd transmembrane region; PRR, proline-rich region; basic, a lysine- and arginine-rich conserved domain. Indicated above the schematic structure are putative key amino acid residues that are conserved in p22phox orthologs, and the residue numbers correspond to those of human p22phox. Detailed alignment of the polybasic region (B) and the PRR (C) are shown. Letters in solid boxes indicate the residues that have been proven by mutational analyses to be important for binding to p47phox and/or activation of human Nox2 [53, 75, 127, 128]. (D) Molecular taxonomy was generated based on the alignment of amino acid sequences of full-length p22phox. Species name abbreviations are given in Figure 3.
###end p 49
###begin p 50
###xml 19 20 19 20 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1</xref>
###xml 27 31 27 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 67 80 67 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus</italic>
###xml 162 166 162 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 197 200 197 200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 292 296 292 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 417 422 417 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 457 462 457 462 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">et al</italic>
###xml 527 532 527 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox-</italic>
###xml 597 601 588 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 617 631 608 622 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 678 681 669 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nox</italic>
###xml 696 698 687 689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B56">56</xref>
###xml 940 942 931 933 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F7">7A</xref>
###xml 1078 1083 1069 1074 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 67 80 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 617 630 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
As shown in Figure 1, a p22phox-like protein was not identified in S. purpuratus, but because the genome sequence of this organism is incomplete and because a p47phox-like protein with a conserved bis-SH3 domain is present, we suggest that this organism probably possesses an undiscovered p22phox-like protein, or a protein that serves an analogous function. Our analysis did not provide convincing evidence for a p22phox isolog in slime mold amoeba. Lardy et al. argued that this organism may possess a membrane-associated p22phox-like protein (GenBanktrade mark accession number ); predicted p22phox-like gene-null D. discoideum mutant is unable to produce spores, similar to nox-null mutants [56]. However according to our analysis, this protein is highly divergent in amino acid sequence compared with the consensus sequence obtained from all other organisms, showing disagreement in 24 out of the 38 conserved residues shown in Figure 7A. Thus, further investigation is needed to judge whether the gene emerged as a later adaptation or whether it represents a primitive p22phox gene.
###end p 50
###begin title 51
Molecular evolution of domains of Nox organizers and activators in Deuterostomia
###end title 51
###begin p 52
###xml 225 226 225 226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 307 312 307 312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 378 379 378 379 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 444 447 444 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 554 555 554 555 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 681 684 681 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 792 794 792 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3C</xref>
###xml 815 826 815 826 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 843 852 843 852 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 895 896 895 896 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 934 945 934 945 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 1023 1028 1023 1028 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1055 1057 1055 1057 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">3B</xref>
###xml 1111 1115 1111 1115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1165 1169 1165 1169 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 815 825 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 843 851 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 934 944 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
As described above, comparisons of the amino acid sequences of the Nox regulatory subunit orthologs revealed certain features of the evolution of characteristic domains. Some key residues and domains are summarized in Figure 8, which shows the proposed evolution of organizer and activator proteins. The p47phox orthologs of all vertebrates (top four left-hand panels in Figure 8) have identical domain structures, which include the PX domain, bis-SH3 domain, AIR, and PRR. On the other hand, the domain composition of NOXO1 (right-hand panels in Figure 8) changed during the evolution from fish to tetrapods: the NOXO1 orthologs of tetrapods and fish all possessed the PX domain, bis-SH3 domain, and PRR. However, the predicted AIR (including key conserved residues, for details, see Figure 3C) is also present in O. latipes but is absent in D. rerio and tetrapods (right-hand panels in Figure 8). Despite the presence of the AIR in O. latipes NOXO1, it is clearly distinguished by sequence homology and synteny from a p47phox isolog, as shown in Figure 3B. Thus, initially, following gene duplication from p47phox, NOXO1 retained the AIR regulatory feature of p47phox, and this feature was subsequently lost.
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 27 32 27 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 46 51 46 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 0 67 0 67 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evolution of domains of p47<italic>phox </italic>/NOXO1 and p67<italic>phox </italic>/NOXA1 orthologs</bold>
###xml 199 203 199 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 217 221 217 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 252 262 252 262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">H. sapiens</italic>
###xml 265 274 265 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G. gallus</italic>
###xml 276 284 276 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio</italic>
###xml 286 296 286 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes</italic>
###xml 298 313 298 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis</italic>
###xml 319 332 319 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus</italic>
###xml 334 346 334 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Solid lines </italic>
###xml 412 425 412 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Broken lines </italic>
###xml 655 661 655 661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox- </italic>

###xml 252 262 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">H. sapiens</span>
###xml 265 274 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 276 284 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 286 296 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>

Evolution of domains of p47phox /NOXO1 and p67phox /NOXA1 orthologs. Shown is a schematic representation of identified domains and known or predicted inter- and intra-molecular interactions among p47phox/NOXO1 and p67phox/NOXA1 orthologs in "mammals" (H. sapiens), G. gallus, D. rerio, O. latipes, C. intestinalis, and S. purpuratus. Broken lines indicate predicted or proposed interactions based on sequences analysis and correspondence to experimentally demonstrated interactions in other species.
