###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 30 34 30 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 43 47 43 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 65 81 65 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 85 99 85 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 122 126 122 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis-</italic>
###xml 256 261 256 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 292 308 292 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 311 316 311 316 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 362 364 362 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B87">87</xref>
###xml 386 390 386 390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 472 477 472 477 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 515 529 506 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 532 536 523 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 664 668 655 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 755 759 737 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 800 801 782 783 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 65 80 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 85 98 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 292 307 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 515 528 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
Like vertebrate isologs of p47phox, the p47phox-like proteins of C. intestinalis and S. purpuratus possess the PX domain, bis-SH3 domain, and AIR. However, these isologs differ considerably in the C-terminal regions that, in higher forms, interact with p67phox isologs. The C-terminus of the C. intestinalis p47phox lacks the PRR, but motif scanning by PROSITE [87] demonstrates the p47phox-like protein contains, instead, additional SH3 domain [residues 340-399 of Ci-p47phox protein, GenBanktrade mark No. ]. The S. purpuratus p47phox-like protein also lacked the C-terminal PRR, but instead had two additional SH3 domains (residues 367-430 and 561-618 of Sp-p47phox, GenBanktrade mark No. ) separated by two PRRs (residues 453-460 and 476-484 of Sp-p47phox) (bottom two left-hand panels in Figure 8).
###end p 54
###begin p 55
###xml 31 36 31 36 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 75 80 75 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 88 89 88 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 125 130 125 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 263 265 263 265 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 266 268 266 268 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 390 395 390 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 396 398 396 398 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 450 455 450 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 492 493 492 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 576 581 576 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 627 643 627 643 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 647 661 647 661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 664 668 664 668 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 721 726 721 726 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 744 745 744 745 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 756 760 756 760 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 852 853 852 853 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 869 883 869 883 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 886 890 886 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1093 1095 1093 1095 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5C</xref>
###xml 1180 1184 1180 1184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 66 71 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 381 386 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 627 642 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 647 660 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 869 882 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
All vertebrate orthologs of p67phox have the same domains seen in human p67phox (Figure 8, left panels). Importantly, all p67phox and NOXA1 proteins possess the AD region, which has been shown to be critical for activating superoxide generation in Nox2 and Nox1 [30,31]. The TPR motif is present in all species, and the two critical residues for Rac-binding, Asp-67 and Arg-102 of human p67phox [21], are conserved among all vertebrate isologs of p67phox and NOXA1 (top four panels in Figure 8), supporting the idea that binding to Rac is a conserved feature of vertebrate p67phox andNOXA1. The N-terminal domain structures of C. intestinalis and S. purpuratus p67phox-like proteins are similar to those of vertebrate p67phox and NOXA1 (Figure 8). Both p67phox-like proteins possess a TPR domain retaining the two critical Rac-binding residues (Figure 8). In addition, S. purpuratus p67phox-like protein possesses a second set of TPR and AD-like domains. Both TRP domains retain conserved essential Rac-binding residues, but the second AD-like domain was not well conserved as shown in Figure 5C. Thus, Rac binding is likely to be an evolutionarily conserved feature among all p67phox/NOXA1 proteins.
###end p 55
###begin p 56
###xml 50 55 50 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 62 67 62 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 184 189 184 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 196 201 196 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 202 204 202 204 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 256 261 256 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 307 311 307 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 349 354 349 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 378 383 378 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 384 386 384 386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B76">76</xref>
###xml 475 480 475 480 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 527 532 527 532 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 569 570 569 570 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 602 606 602 606 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 700 701 700 701 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 750 755 750 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 756 758 756 758 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 782 791 782 791 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G. gallus</italic>
###xml 806 815 806 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. rerio </italic>
###xml 819 830 819 830 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 900 905 900 905 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 913 914 913 914 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F6">6</xref>
###xml 958 963 958 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1072 1077 1072 1077 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1151 1152 1151 1152 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 1188 1193 1188 1193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1239 1255 1239 1255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 1259 1273 1259 1273 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 1276 1280 1276 1280 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1348 1353 1348 1353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 247 252 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 340 345 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 774 781 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">chicken</span>
###xml 782 791 <span type="species:ncbi:9031">G. gallus</span>
###xml 806 814 <span type="species:ncbi:7955">D. rerio</span>
###xml 819 829 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 1239 1254 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 1259 1272 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
In mammals, binding between the PB1 domains of p67phox and p40phox has been shown to mediate heterodimer formation. The crystal structure of the heterodimer of the PB1 domains from p67phox and p40phox [32] demonstrated that Lys-355 and Lys-382 in human p67phox are essential to bind to the PB1 domain of p40phox, and mutation of Lys-355 of human p67phox abolished binding to p40phox [76]. These crucial residues are entirely conserved in the PB1 domains of all vertebrate p67phox proteins, which imply that they all bind to p40phox (top four left-hand panels in Figure 8). In contrast to vertebrate p67phox, mammalian NOXA1 does not retain these two key amino acids (a top right-hand panel of Figure 8), explaining the failure of NOXA1 to bind to p40phox [40]. However, the chicken G. gallus, and the fish D. rerio and O. latipes NOXA1 completely conserve these two residues, and an OPCA motif of p40phox (Figure 6), which is essential for binding to the p67phox PB1 domain are highly conserved. The conservations of key residues suggest that in these fish, binding to p40phox may be retained (from the second to fourth panels in right hand of Figure 8). Thus, the loss of function of p40phox can be traced in the evolution of NOXA1. Both C. intestinalis and S. purpuratus p67phox-like proteins lack a PB1 domain, consistent with the absence of p40phox orthologs.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 26 31 26 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 65 67 65 67 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 68 70 68 70 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 71 73 71 73 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B79">79</xref>
###xml 74 76 74 76 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B80">80</xref>
###xml 93 98 93 98 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 180 182 180 182 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 183 185 183 185 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B81">81</xref>
###xml 186 188 186 188 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B88">88</xref>
###xml 191 203 191 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">T. rubripes </italic>
###xml 206 211 206 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 291 293 291 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B89">89</xref>
###xml 521 526 521 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 553 556 553 556 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e.g</italic>
###xml 632 637 632 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 17 22 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 191 202 <span type="species:ncbi:31033">T. rubripes</span>
The PX-domain of human p40phox specifically binds to PtdIns(3)P [23,24,79,80]. Therefore, p40phox accumulates during phagocytosis at early endosomes, which are rich in PtdIns(3)P [35,81,88]. T. rubripes p40phox is expressed in a wide range of tissues including the gastrointestinal tissues [89], while Nox2 expression is restricted to the blood and kidney. Although Nox1 expression in fish or the other non-mammal organisms is not clear, our analysis suggest that Nox1 of fish and birds might function, along with the p40phox orthologs, in endocytosis, e.g., in receptor-internalization. This novel relationship between Nox1 and p40phox may provide a clue to understanding the physiological role of Nox1 in vertebrates.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 18 23 18 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 128 133 128 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 446 450 446 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 459 463 459 463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 481 497 481 497 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 504 518 504 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 605 609 605 609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 648 652 648 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 712 713 712 713 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 776 792 776 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. intestinalis </italic>
###xml 795 799 795 799 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 841 846 841 846 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 924 928 915 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 982 983 973 974 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 1150 1164 1141 1155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus </italic>
###xml 1167 1171 1158 1162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1253 1263 1244 1254 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpura</italic>
###xml 1270 1274 1261 1265 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1333 1338 1324 1329 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1345 1350 1336 1341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1422 1423 1413 1414 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 1767 1771 1758 1762 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2098 2103 2089 2094 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2140 2145 2131 2136 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2169 2170 2160 2161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 87 92 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 481 496 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 504 517 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 776 791 <span type="species:ncbi:7719">C. intestinalis</span>
###xml 1150 1163 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 1253 1266 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
The vertebrate p67phox and NOXA1 orthologs all have the C-terminal SH3 domain that, in human, mediates binding to the PRR of p47phox and NOXO1, respectively. This supports the idea that all of the vertebrate forms of these proteins mediate protein interactions via tail-to-tail binding between the SH3 domain of the activator protein and the PRR of the organizer protein. We further suggest that even though the structures of the C-termini of p47phox- and p67phox-like proteins in C. intestinalis and in S. purpuratus differ from the vertebrate proteins, the same sort of tail-to-tail binding of these p67phox-like proteins to the corresponding p47phox-like proteins occurs as diagrammed at the bottom of Figure 8. For example, we suggest that the C-terminal putative PRRs of C. intestinalis p67phox-like proteins (residues 256-348 of Ci-p67phox protein, GenBanktrade mark No. ) binds to the C-terminal SH3 domain of the p47phox-like protein as indicated by a broken line in Figure 8, reversing the mode of interaction seen in the vertebrate proteins but accomplishing the same function. Similarly, SH3 domains and putative PRRs in the C-terminus of S. purpuratus p47phox-like protein may interact with the PRRs and the SH3 domains in the C-terminus of S. purpuratus p67phox, respectively. Thus, while domains in the C-termini of p47phox and p67phox orthologs are not conserved during evolution, the model shown in Figure 8 suggests that the "docking function" has been retained. The model suggests three functional modules within the organizer protein/activator protein complex: 1), a "membrane-binding/cytochrome docking region" on the organizer protein that is comprised of the phospholipids-binding PX domain and the tandem SH3 region that binds to the PRR of p22phox; 2) a "Nox-activating region" that contains the Rac-binding TPR domain and the AD, which together cooperate to stimulate the activity of the Nox catalytic domain; and 3) a "regulator-docking region" which uses evolutionarily variable but paired docking modules that link the "membrane-binding/cytochrome docking region" of p47phox to the "Nox-activating region" of p67phox (bottom panel in Figure 8).
###end p 58
###begin title 59
###xml 25 29 25 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
Occurrence and origin of Phox-like regulatory subunits during evolution of Metazoa and Choanoflagellata
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 230 253 230 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Nematostella vectensis </italic>
###xml 254 266 254 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. vectensis</italic>
###xml 280 296 280 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Lottia gigantea </italic>
###xml 297 308 297 308 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">L. gigantea</italic>
###xml 339 360 339 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Monosiga brevicollis </italic>
###xml 361 375 361 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis</italic>
###xml 399 400 399 400 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S5">5</xref>
###xml 402 403 402 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S6">6</xref>
###xml 405 406 405 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 408 409 408 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S8">8</xref>
###xml 511 513 511 513 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B90">90</xref>
###xml 640 651 640 651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">L. gigantea</italic>
###xml 691 695 691 695 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 700 704 700 704 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 709 713 709 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 758 760 758 760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A</xref>
###xml 834 836 834 836 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9B</xref>
###xml 866 871 866 871 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 910 915 910 915 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1025 1026 1025 1026 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S8">8</xref>
###xml 1057 1069 1057 1069 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">L. gigantea </italic>
###xml 1153 1155 1153 1155 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A</xref>
###xml 1180 1181 1180 1181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S6">6</xref>
###xml 1229 1230 1229 1230 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 1373 1396 1373 1396 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Caenorhabditis elegans </italic>
###xml 1400 1423 1400 1423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Caenorhabditis briggsae</italic>
###xml 1440 1463 1440 1463 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila melanogaster</italic>
###xml 1465 1479 1465 1479 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Apis mellifera</italic>
###xml 1481 1498 1481 1498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Anopheles gambiae</italic>
###xml 1500 1512 1500 1512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Aedes aegypt</italic>
###xml 1559 1572 1559 1572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Daphnia pulex</italic>
###xml 1582 1584 1582 1584 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A</xref>
###xml 230 252 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">Nematostella vectensis</span>
###xml 254 266 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 280 295 <span type="species:ncbi:225164">Lottia gigantea</span>
###xml 297 308 <span type="species:ncbi:225164">L. gigantea</span>
###xml 339 359 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">Monosiga brevicollis</span>
###xml 361 375 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 640 651 <span type="species:ncbi:225164">L. gigantea</span>
###xml 1057 1068 <span type="species:ncbi:225164">L. gigantea</span>
###xml 1373 1395 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">Caenorhabditis elegans</span>
###xml 1400 1423 <span type="species:ncbi:6238">Caenorhabditis briggsae</span>
###xml 1440 1463 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila melanogaster</span>
###xml 1465 1479 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">Apis mellifera</span>
###xml 1481 1498 <span type="species:ncbi:7165">Anopheles gambiae</span>
###xml 1559 1572 <span type="species:ncbi:6669">Daphnia pulex</span>
In addition to regulatory subunit-dependent Nox proteins of the Deuterostomia, we assembled predicted regulatory subunits and the subunit-regulated Nox isolog sequences present in the genomes of following species: the sea anemone Nematostella vectensis (N. vectensis), the limpet Lottia gigantea (L. gigantea), the marine choanoflagellate Monosiga brevicollis (M. brevicollis) (see Additional files 5, 6, 7, 8). According to the recent phylogeny based on small ribosomal subunit gene and other molecular tools [90], the bilaterian animals consist of three clades: Deuterostomia, Lophotrochozoa, and Ecdysozoa. A gastropod snail, the limpet L. gigantea, belongs to the Lophotrochozoa, and p67phox, p47phox, p22phox-like genes are found in this genome (Figure 9A). The predicted motif structures by the Pfam program are shown in Figure 9B; characteristic motifs of p67phox (TPR domain and AD-like region) and p47phox (PX domain and AIR-like region) as well as the key residues (detailed alignments are shown in Additional file 8) are conserved. The genome of L. gigantea also possesses an ancestral Nox2 gene as a co-ortholog of vertebrate Nox1-3 (Figure 9A and see Additional file 6) like Nox2 isologs in primitive deuterostomes [1]. On the other hand, any distinct regulatory subunit genes were not found in seven species that belongs to Ecdysozoa including two nemotodes (Caenorhabditis elegans and Caenorhabditis briggsae), four insects (Drosophila melanogaster, Apis mellifera, Anopheles gambiae, Aedes aegypt), and one non-insect arthropod (the waterflea Daphnia pulex) (Figure 9A).
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 71 76 71 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox </italic>
###xml 0 104 0 104 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Relationship between the evolution of eukaryotes and the occurrence of <italic>Phox </italic>-related regulatory subunits</bold>
###xml 107 108 107 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 604 605 604 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 779 780 779 780 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S7">7</xref>
###xml 908 919 908 919 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Underlines </italic>
###xml 1005 1018 1005 1018 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Bold letters </italic>
###xml 1099 1109 1099 1109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">H. sapiens</italic>
###xml 1115 1128 1115 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. purpuratus</italic>
###xml 1130 1146 1130 1146 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Nv, N. vectensis</italic>
###xml 1152 1163 1152 1163 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">L. gigantea</italic>

Relationship between the evolution of eukaryotes and the occurrence of Phox -related regulatory subunits. (A) A phylogeny of eukaryotes was created based largely on genetic information [90, 100]. Branch lengths are for illustrative purposes and are not proportional to phylogenetic distances of groups. Details of deusterostomes are shown in Figure 1. "n.i." indicates none identified or reported. "co-ortho. of v-Nox1-3" indicates that the gene is a co-ortholog ancestor of all members of the vertebrate Nox1-3 subgroup. The number in a parenthesis (e.g. [129, 130, 131]) indicates a reference number. (B) Predicted domains structures of newly identified putative regulatory subunit-like proteins are shown; P, proline-rich region. The sequences are provided in Additional file 7. ###begin p 62
###xml 178 180 178 180 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B90">90</xref>
###xml 207 220 207 220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. vectensis </italic>
###xml 263 267 263 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 273 277 273 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 341 343 341 343 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A</xref>
###xml 462 464 462 464 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9B</xref>
###xml 506 507 506 507 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S8">8</xref>
###xml 510 523 510 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. vectensis </italic>
###xml 526 531 526 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 548 551 548 551 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 680 685 680 685 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 770 772 770 772 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B91">91</xref>
###xml 889 902 889 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. vectensis </italic>
###xml 939 943 939 943 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 995 1008 995 1008 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. vectensis </italic>
###xml 1011 1016 1011 1016 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1045 1050 1045 1050 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1163 1176 1163 1176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. vectensis </italic>
###xml 1407 1409 1403 1405 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B92">92</xref>
###xml 1464 1468 1460 1464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 187 206 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">starlet sea anemone</span>
###xml 207 219 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 510 522 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 671 676 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 889 901 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 995 1007 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 1163 1175 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
Before the emergence of bilateral animals, cnidarians split from the main animal lineage and the genome retained many of the features present in last common ancestor of animals [90]. The starlet sea anemone N. vectensis that belongs to the Cnidaria, conserves p47phox-, p22phox-like genes, and two ancestral Nox2 genes, Nox2A and 2B (Figure 9A). The characteristic motifs of the putative regulatory subunits are predicted by the Pfam program and shown in Figure 9B (alignments are shown in Additional file 8). N. vectensis p47phox possesses PX and bis-SH3 domains. The isolog also possesses a putative polybasic region within the sequence corresponding to the AIR of the human p47phox gene. A polybasic region is a class III consensus motif for binding to a SH3 domain [91]; therefore, this may implicate the polybasic region as a prototype of the AIR. Although the current version of the N. vectensis genome does not encode an obvious p67phox-like gene, the presence of multiple SH3 domains in N. vectensis p47phox points to an unidentified p67phox ortholog or an unknown PRR-containing binding partner. Although cnidarians have no specialized immune cells, the N. vectensis genome possesses orthologous genes to Toll/Toll-like receptors, complement C3-like molecules, and a redox-sensitive transcription factor nuclear factor-kappaB that are orthologs of key components of innate immunity in vertebrates [92]. Further study needs to identify an original role of Phox-type NADPH oxidase in the primitive multicellular animals.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 160 164 160 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 409 411 409 411 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B93">93</xref>
###xml 427 429 427 429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B94">94</xref>
###xml 619 621 619 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B90">90</xref>
###xml 622 624 622 624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B95">95</xref>
###xml 625 627 625 627 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B96">96</xref>
###xml 793 808 793 808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 966 968 966 968 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B97">97</xref>
###xml 969 971 969 971 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B98">98</xref>
###xml 1003 1018 1003 1018 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 1031 1035 1031 1035 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1044 1048 1044 1048 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1069 1073 1069 1073 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A,B</xref>
###xml 1113 1128 1113 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 1179 1184 1179 1184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1240 1255 1240 1255 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 1279 1281 1279 1281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A</xref>
###xml 1343 1358 1343 1358 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 1575 1576 1575 1576 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S6">6</xref>
###xml 1583 1598 1583 1598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 1601 1605 1601 1605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1763 1765 1763 1765 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9C</xref>
###xml 2013 2028 2013 2028 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 2072 2076 2072 2076 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 793 807 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 1003 1017 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 1113 1127 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 1240 1254 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 1343 1357 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 1583 1597 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 2013 2027 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
One clear implication of these genomic and detailed sequence analyses described above is that the hypothetical ancestor of primitive animals might conserve the Phox-type NADPH-oxidase system. In the middle of the nineteenth century, a striking structural resemblance between the collar cells, so-called "choanocytes", of primitive animal sponges and a group of protists the choanoflagellates has been noted ([93], reviewed in [94]). A line of recent phylogenic analyses suggests that the metazoa including sponges, cnidarians, and other animals constitutes a monophyletic clade closely related to the Choanoflagellata [90,95,96]; therefore, the choanoflagellates are considered to be the organisms that are close in evolution to the all modern animals. The unicellular marine choanoflagellate M. brevicollis has been reported as a closer relatives to the hypothetical ancestor of all multicellular animals based on the comparative analyses of animal-specific genes [97,98]. Interestingly, the genome of M. brevicollis possesses p47phox- and p22phox-like genes (Figures 9A,B), but a BLAST searching in the current M. brevicollis genomic database failed to identify a dinstinct p67phox ortholog. Furthermore, Nox2-like gene is present in the M. brevicollis genome sequence (Figure 9A). Interestingly, a taxonomy of Nox domains demonstrates that M. brevicollis Nox2-like gene diverges from the monophyletic clade of all metazoan Nox2 genes containing other ancestral Nox2 and all vertebrate Nox1-3, but it differs from Nox4 and fungal NoxA/NoxB subfamilies (see Additional file 6). The M. brevicollis p47phox-like protein possesses AIR-like region that conserves a serine residue consistent with a consensus motif of a putative substrate of protein kinase C (Figure 9C); therefore, this implies that ROS-generating activity of the most primitive Nox2-like protein is also strictly regulated by phosphorylation as seen in mammalian phagocyte NADPH-oxidase. The physiological function of the primordial Nox2 enzyme in M. brevicollis is unknown, but the early appearance of the Phox-like Nox system in the unicellular flagellate suggests the presence of a fundamental and essential role of the regulatory subunit-dependent Nox in a unicellular living.
###end p 63

###xml 2375 2386 2375 2386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N. gruberi </italic>

###xml 413 426 <span type="species:ncbi:7668">S. purpuratus</span>
###xml 569 580 <span type="species:ncbi:225164">L. gigantea</span>
###xml 596 608 <span type="species:ncbi:45351">N. vectensis</span>
###xml 873 894 <span type="species:ncbi:3218">Physcomitrella patens</span>
###xml 896 905 <span type="species:ncbi:3218">P. patens</span>
###xml 976 996 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">Arabidopsis thaliana</span>
###xml 998 1009 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 1015 1027 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">Oryza sativa</span>
###xml 1029 1038 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">O. sativa</span>
###xml 1106 1124 <span type="species:ncbi:67593">Phytophthora sojae</span>
###xml 1126 1134 <span type="species:ncbi:67593">P. sojae</span>
###xml 1267 1276 <span type="species:ncbi:3218">P. patens</span>
###xml 1281 1289 <span type="species:ncbi:67593">P. sojae</span>
###xml 1691 1708 <span type="species:ncbi:5762">Naegleria gruberi</span>
###xml 1710 1720 <span type="species:ncbi:5762">N. gruberi</span>
###xml 1852 1862 <span type="species:ncbi:5762">N. gruberi</span>
###xml 1975 1988 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 1993 2014 <span type="species:ncbi:5759">Entamoeba histolytica</span>
###xml 2062 2079 <span type="species:ncbi:5763">Naegleria fowleri</span>
###xml 2149 2159 <span type="species:ncbi:5762">N. gruberi</span>
###xml 2375 2385 <span type="species:ncbi:5762">N. gruberi</span>
###xml 2402 2415 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 2492 2502 <span type="species:ncbi:5762">N. gruberi</span>
Figure 9A also summarizes the occurrence of Nox4, Nox5, and Duox isologs in genomes of the metazoa and the choanoflagellate, adding to information published previously [1]. Duox orthologs are present in all analyzed genomes of the Bilateria (Figure 9A). Nox5 genes occur broadly in the genomes of Metazoa, but not in Nematoda. Nox4 genes appear after the emergence of chordates, but is not seen in the echinoderm S. purpuratus [1] (Figure 1A). Interestingly, gene search that covers a wide range demonstrates that Nox4-like genes are also present in a lophotrochozoan (L. gigantea), a cnidarian (N. vectensis), but not in the ecdysozoans (see Figure 9A, and the taxonomy of Nox is shown in Additional file 6). The choanoflagellate M. brevicolli do not possess Nox4, Nox5, and Duox orthologs, at least based on the current genomic database. In the kingdom Plantae, the moss Physcomitrella patens (P. patens) possess double EF-hand- containing Noxes like the higher land plants Arabidopsis thaliana (A. thaliana) and Oryza sativa (O. sativa) (Figure 9A). Despite a kingdom distinct from plants, the oomycete Phytophthora sojae (P. sojae) also possesses single or double EF-hand(s)-containing Noxes [55,99], at least three genes (Figure 9A). Here we referred to them as P. patens and P. sojae rboh (respiratory burst oxidase homolog) to represent the remarkable resemblance to the higher plant Noxes, so-called rboh, in the respects of taxonomy of the Nox domains (Additional file 6). In the kingdoms Plantae and Chomista, a distinct regulatory subunit was not seen. However, higher plant genomes possess a novel protein family conserved domain structures similar to p67phox as descried below. Naegleria gruberi (N. gruberi) is a widespread soil and freshwater amoeboflagellate that belongs to the phylum Perocolozoa, the kingdom Protozoa [100]. Although N. gruberi is a free-living organism, it is not related to species of the phylum Amoebozoa with sequenced genomes, such as D. discoideum and Entamoeba histolytica, but it is close to pathogenic relatives (e.g. Naegleria fowleri) that can cause amoebic meningitis. We identified single Nox gene of N. gruberi from the genome (Figure 9A), together with five putative Fre ortholog genes that have similar domain structures to that of Nox domain (see Additional file 9). According to a phylogenetic taxonomy of Nox domain, the N. gruberi Nox is close to D. discoideum NoxA/NoxB proteins (see Additional file 6); therefore, it is referred to as N. gruberi NoxA (Figure 9A). Nox regulatory subunit gene has not been found in the current version of genomic database, but it might contain a prototype of regulatory subunits according to the Nox taxonomy.
###end p 64
###begin title 65
###xml 16 21 16 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
SH3PXD2 as a p47phox family member
###end title 65
###begin p 66
###xml 19 20 19 20 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9</xref>
###xml 74 78 74 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 138 143 138 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 223 237 223 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicolli </italic>
###xml 240 244 240 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 347 352 347 352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 384 385 384 385 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">"</bold>
###xml 484 486 484 486 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S10">10</xref>
###xml 491 493 491 493 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S11">11</xref>
###xml 583 586 583 586 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis</italic>
###xml 714 717 714 717 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">10A</xref>
###xml 846 849 846 849 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">10A</xref>
###xml 854 857 854 857 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">10B</xref>
###xml 924 927 924 927 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">10A</xref>
###xml 948 963 948 963 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevicollis </italic>
###xml 966 970 966 970 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1011 1015 1011 1015 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1108 1113 1108 1113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1143 1146 1143 1146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">10A</xref>
###xml 1367 1370 1367 1370 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B101">101</xref>
###xml 1371 1374 1371 1374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B102">102</xref>
###xml 1570 1573 1570 1573 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B101">101</xref>
###xml 2003 2019 2003 2019 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. brevilcollis </italic>
###xml 2022 2026 2022 2026 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2071 2076 2071 2076 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2144 2148 2144 2148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 2223 2226 2223 2226 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F10">10B</xref>
###xml 2247 2252 2247 2252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 2377 2378 2377 2378 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 948 962 <span type="species:ncbi:81824">M. brevicollis</span>
###xml 1223 1228 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1554 1559 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
As shown in Figure 9, a choanoflagellate and primitive animals possess p47phox-like genes as well as ancestral Nox2 and PRR-containing p22phox genes. On the other hand, further BLASTP search in the animal genomes using the M. brevicolli p47phox-like protein sequence suggested the presence of a protein family proteins related to the primitive p47phox in higher animals, encoding the "SH3 and PX domains 2" protein (SH3PXD2) (sequences and alignments are provided in Additional files 10 and 11, respectively). The encoded protein is composed of an N-terminal PX domain and a central bis-SH3 domain, plus two or three additional SH3 domains in the C-terminal half of the molecule (see the motif structure in Figure 10A). The SH3PXD2 gene is present in a urochordate, but was not seen in an echinoderm and other primitive metazoan species (Figures 10A and 10B). In vertebrates, two isozymes SH3PXD2a and 2b were found (Figure 10A). Interestingly the M. brevicollis p47phox-like gene and other primitive animal p47phox-like genes are related more closely to the SH3PXD2 gene subfamily than to the vertebrate p47phox and NOXO1 subfamilies (Figure 10A). The physiological function of SH3PXD2a is suggested by only a few papers; human SH3PXD2a protein (a.k.a. Tks5) is involved in the protease-driven invasion of cancer cells and the neurotoxicity induced by amyloid-beta [101,102]. A protein binding to SH3PXD2a is also little known, but recently N-WASP (Wiskott-Aldrich Syndrome protein) was proposed as a candidate that binds to the third SH3 domain of the human SH3PXD2a [101]. The physiological role as well as the binding partner of SH3PXD2b is unknown. However, the clear phylogenetic relationship of the SH3PXD2 gene family to the larger family of Nox-regulatory organizing proteins suggests that the genes might be involved in regulating Nox activity. Alternatively, SH3PXD2 proteins may have diverged to perform unrelated functions (e.g., to regulate other enzymes or signaling pathways). Thus, the M. brevilcollis p47phox-like protein evolved from a hypothetical p47phox ancestor, and the SH3PXD2 genes diverged from the lineage of the p47phox-like gene following the emergence of chordates but prior to NOXO1 (Figure 10B). The vertebrate p47phox and NOXO1 were somehow able to eliminate the additional SH3 domains in the "regulator-docking region", as proposed in Figure 8.
###end p 66

###begin title 68
What is the regulatory subunit binding partner for fungal NOXR?
###end title 68
###begin p 69
###xml 7 18 7 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. nidulans</italic>
###xml 20 29 20 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. grisea</italic>
###xml 35 49 35 49 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F. graminearum</italic>
###xml 73 75 73 75 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 111 116 111 116 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 133 135 133 135 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F9">9A</xref>
###xml 189 193 189 193 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 235 240 235 240 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 261 263 261 263 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 285 287 285 287 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5E</xref>
###xml 519 522 519 522 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11A</xref>
###xml 605 608 605 608 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B103">103</xref>
###xml 630 641 630 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. nidulans</italic>
###xml 643 652 643 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. grisea</italic>
###xml 658 673 658 673 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F. graminearum </italic>
###xml 740 745 740 745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 965 968 956 959 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11B</xref>
###xml 993 995 984 986 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S12">12</xref>
###xml 1248 1251 1239 1242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11C</xref>
###xml 7 18 <span type="species:ncbi:162425">A. nidulans</span>
###xml 20 29 <span type="species:ncbi:148305">M. grisea</span>
###xml 35 49 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">F. graminearum</span>
###xml 630 641 <span type="species:ncbi:162425">A. nidulans</span>
###xml 643 652 <span type="species:ncbi:148305">M. grisea</span>
###xml 658 672 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">F. graminearum</span>
###xml 731 736 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Fungi (A. nidulans, M. grisea, and F. graminearum) belong to Ascomycota [55] and possess the NOXR gene as a p67phox ortholog (Figure 9A). NOXR encodes a PB1 domain homologous to that in p67phox, but these organisms do not possess a p40phox ortholog (see Figure 1A). As shown in Figure 5E, two important basic residues in the PB1 domains are conserved in all NOXR proteins. The conservation of these residues implies the existence of an unknown NOXR binding partner(s) containing a PB1 domain with an OPCA motif (Figure 11A). A BLAST search of a database of computationally predicted amino acid sequences [103] from the genomes of A. nidulans, M. grisea, and F. graminearum was performed using as a query sequence the PB1 domain of human p40phox (residues 237-339; GenBanktrade mark No. ). In addition to NOXR, three sequences harboring PB1 domains were identified in the fungi. These were: "SH3-SH3-PX-SRR-PB1", "CDC24-RhoGEF-PB1" and "(CBS)n-PB1" proteins (Figure 11B and see Additional file 12), so-named for their domain structures in sequence from N- to C-termini. SRR indicates a serine-rich region. The three predicted proteins were encoded in all three fungal genomes, and all three possessed acidic OPCA motifs in their PB1 domains (Figure 11C).
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 0 77 0 77 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Predicted binding partners of fungal NOXR and activation models of fungal Nox</bold>
###xml 80 81 80 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 154 155 154 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 339 350 330 341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. nidulans</italic>
###xml 356 365 347 356 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">M. grisea</italic>
###xml 371 385 362 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F. graminearum</italic>
###xml 388 389 379 380 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 487 492 478 483 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 627 636 618 627 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">asterisks</italic>
###xml 639 640 630 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 715 716 706 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E</italic>
###xml 784 785 775 776 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F</italic>
###xml 339 350 <span type="species:ncbi:162425">A. nidulans</span>
###xml 356 365 <span type="species:ncbi:148305">M. grisea</span>
###xml 371 385 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">F. graminearum</span>
###xml 500 505 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>

(B) Domain structures of fungal proteins with PB1 domains meeting criteria for possible NOXR-partners are shown, along with their GenBanktrade mark accession numbers. Abbreviations: An, A. nidulans; Mg, M. grisea; Fg, F. graminearum. ###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 78 92 78 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 192 206 183 197 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 245 247 236 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B76">76</xref>
###xml 343 346 334 337 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11D</xref>
###xml 451 456 442 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 463 468 454 459 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 606 607 597 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F8">8</xref>
###xml 626 640 617 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 704 707 695 698 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B104">104</xref>
###xml 748 753 739 744 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 774 776 765 767 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">1A</xref>
###xml 873 875 864 866 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B91">91</xref>
###xml 1007 1008 998 999 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 1050 1054 1041 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bis-</italic>
###xml 1181 1195 1172 1186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 1247 1250 1238 1241 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B105">105</xref>
###xml 72 77 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
###xml 78 91 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 192 205 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 626 639 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1181 1194 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
The "SH3-SH3-PX-SRR-PB1" protein contains a similar domain structure to yeast S. cerevisiae Bem1p (Bud Emergence 1, GenBanktrade mark accession number ), but differs in that the PB1 domain of S. cerevisiae Bem1p does not contain the OPCA motif [76]. A speculative model for the regulation of fungal Nox by the Bem1 ortholog is shown in Figure 11D, wherein Bem1 ortholog is proposed to play a role as an organizer protein, analogous to the roles of p47phox and p40phox in mammals. According to this model, PB1-PB1 interaction mediates the linkage between the "regulator-docking regions" suggested in Figure 8. PX-domain of the S. cerevisiae Bem1 facilitates a protein to anchor to a membrane lipid layer [104]. Fungi do not have a PRR-containing p22phox ortholog (see Figure 1A), but NoxA and NoxB in the three fungi has a distinctive highly conserved a class II PRR motif [91] (e.g. 423-428 residues of Mg-NoxA) and class III (e.g. 447-452 residues of Mg-NoxB) near the predicted NADPH-binding sub-regions [1]. Thus the hypothetical functions of the bis-SH3 and PX domains indicate the analogous function as a "membrane-binding/cytochrome docking region" of Nox organizer. Because S. cerevisiae Bem1 is involved in establishment of cell polarity [105], the proposed interaction between fungal NOXR and Bem1 orthologs may point to a function of Nox-derived ROS in cell polarity.
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 87 101 87 101 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 328 331 319 322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11E</xref>
###xml 451 453 442 444 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
###xml 87 100 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
A second model is suggested by the "CDC24-RhoGEF-PB1" protein, which is an ortholog of S. cerevisiae Cdc24p (GenBanktrade mark accession number ). According to this "exchanger model", the PB1-mediated heterodimer formation localizes the RhoGEF domain which then catalyzes the conversion of Rac-GDP to the active Rac-GTP (Figure 11E). The model is supported by a recent report showed that fungal NOXR binds to the fungal Rac homologue in the GTP form [57].
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 56 59 56 59 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11F</xref>
###xml 390 393 390 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B106">106</xref>
###xml 394 397 394 397 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B107">107</xref>
An "energy sensor" function for NOXR is shown in Figure 11F, and is based on the occurrence of the CBS (cystathione beta-synthase) domain in the putative binding partner. The CBS domain senses cellular energy status by binding adenosine nucleotides; it occurs in a range of proteins including AMP-activated protein kinase, which is activated by AMP and inhibited by ATP via the CBS domain [106,107]. Such a function might be related to the requirement of Nox enzyme for reduced pyridine nucleotide, thus affecting cellular energetics.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 110 112 110 112 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 201 203 201 203 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F11">11</xref>
###xml 433 435 433 435 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S12">12</xref>
###xml 544 575 544 575 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Batrachochytrium dendrobatidis </italic>
###xml 576 592 576 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B. dendrobatidis</italic>
###xml 666 680 666 680 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Y. lipolytica </italic>
###xml 689 709 689 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Coprinopsis cinerea </italic>
###xml 751 753 751 753 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F12">12</xref>
###xml 815 828 815 828 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae</italic>
###xml 884 922 884 922 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Candida albicans, Yarrowia lipolytica </italic>
###xml 923 936 923 936 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Y. lipolytica</italic>
###xml 942 968 942 968 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Schizosaccharomyces pombe </italic>
###xml 969 977 969 977 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. pombe</italic>
###xml 980 982 980 982 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 1024 1038 1024 1038 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Y. lipolytica </italic>
###xml 1042 1067 1042 1067 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phycomyces blakesleeanus </italic>
###xml 1068 1084 1068 1084 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">P. blakesleeanus</italic>
###xml 1124 1126 1124 1126 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B55">55</xref>
###xml 1133 1150 1133 1150 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">P. blakesleeanus </italic>
###xml 1361 1366 1361 1366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1487 1491 1487 1491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1768 1782 1768 1782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">S. cerevisiae </italic>
###xml 1786 1798 1786 1798 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. albicans </italic>
###xml 1820 1822 1820 1822 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F12">12</xref>
###xml 1894 1896 1894 1896 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S13">13</xref>
###xml 1901 1903 1901 1903 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S14">14</xref>
###xml 544 574 <span type="species:ncbi:109871">Batrachochytrium dendrobatidis</span>
###xml 576 592 <span type="species:ncbi:109871">B. dendrobatidis</span>
###xml 666 679 <span type="species:ncbi:4952">Y. lipolytica</span>
###xml 689 708 <span type="species:ncbi:5346">Coprinopsis cinerea</span>
###xml 815 828 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 884 900 <span type="species:ncbi:5476">Candida albicans</span>
###xml 902 921 <span type="species:ncbi:4952">Yarrowia lipolytica</span>
###xml 923 936 <span type="species:ncbi:4952">Y. lipolytica</span>
###xml 942 967 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">Schizosaccharomyces pombe</span>
###xml 969 977 <span type="species:ncbi:4896">S. pombe</span>
###xml 1024 1037 <span type="species:ncbi:4952">Y. lipolytica</span>
###xml 1042 1066 <span type="species:ncbi:4837">Phycomyces blakesleeanus</span>
###xml 1068 1084 <span type="species:ncbi:4837">P. blakesleeanus</span>
###xml 1133 1149 <span type="species:ncbi:4837">P. blakesleeanus</span>
###xml 1352 1357 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1478 1483 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 1768 1781 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">S. cerevisiae</span>
###xml 1786 1797 <span type="species:ncbi:5476">C. albicans</span>
Fungal Nox and NOXR isologs are seen not only in fungi belonging to Ascomycota, but also some basidiomycetes [55]. To explore the likelihood of the fungal Nox activation mechanisms suggested in Figure 11, the occurrence of NOXR, Bem1, Cdc24, and CBSn-PB1 isologs were compared in 13 fungal genomes spanning the four fungal divisions: Ascomycota, Basidiomycota, Zygomycota, and Chytridiomycota (sequences are shown in Additional file 12). Bem1, Cdc24, and CBSn-PB1 genes are present in most of the fungal genomes, with the exception of Cdc24 in Batrachochytrium dendrobatidis (B. dendrobatidis), and these proteins all conserved the PB1 domains with some exceptions; Y. lipolytica NOXR and Coprinopsis cinerea Cdc24 isologs lack the PB1 domain (Figure 12). In addition to the absence of Nox and NOXR isolog genes in S. cerevisiae, the Nox and NOXR isologs are absent in the genomes of Candida albicans, Yarrowia lipolytica (Y. lipolytica) and Schizosaccharomyces pombe (S. pombe) [55]. A Nox gene is absent in the genomes of Y. lipolytica and Phycomyces blakesleeanus (P. blakesleeanus) despite the presence of NOXR isologs [55]. The P. blakesleeanus genome possesses two Bem1 and CBS-PB1 genes and all conserved the PB1 domains. We investigated the conservation of two basic residues of the PB1 domain corresponding to the Lys-355 and -382 residues of human p67phox and the four acidic residues in OPCA motif corresponding to the Asp-289, Glu-291, and Asp-293, -302 residues of human p40phox. Comparison of the PB1 domains in these fungal proteins by alignment and analyses by the Pfam program demonstrate that the two basic and four acidic residues are conserved in the fungal NOXR, Bem1, Cdc24, and CBSn-PB1 with a few exceptions; the OPCA motifs in Bem1 isologs of S. cerevisiae and C. albicans has been lost (Figure 12 and the sequences and detailed alignments are shown in Additional file 13 and 14, respectively). The high conservation of the motif strongly implies that these PB1 domains mediate functionally important oligomerizations. Future functional studies will clarify the roles of these proteins in fungal Nox functions.
###end p 74
###begin p 75
###xml 0 115 0 115 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Conservations of NOXR, Bem1, Cdc24, and CBSn-PB1 genes and characteristic residues of PB1 domains in fungal genomes</bold>
###xml 118 119 118 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 337 342 337 342 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 448 452 448 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">bold</italic>

###end p 75
###begin title 76
###xml 31 45 31 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 31 44 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
Predicted binding partners for D. discoideum p67-like protein
###end title 76
###begin p 77
###xml 37 51 37 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 152 154 152 154 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">5E</xref>
###xml 193 207 193 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 362 364 362 364 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F13">13</xref>
###xml 401 403 401 403 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S15">15</xref>
###xml 464 478 464 478 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 511 514 507 510 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B108">108</xref>
###xml 748 750 744 746 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 751 754 747 750 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B109">109</xref>
###xml 755 758 751 754 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B111">111</xref>
###xml 37 50 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 193 206 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
###xml 464 477 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
Like fungal NOXRs, the PB1 domain of D. discoideum p67-like protein also possesses two basic residues, Lys-313 and Lys-340 residues, as shown in Figure 5E. A BLAST search demonstrates that the D. discoideum genome possesses five predicted PB1 domain-containing proteins (referred to here as "Dd-PB1-A to -E"). All except Dd-PB1-D conserve the OPCA motif (Figure 13, and see details in Additional file 15). Dd-PB1-A protein (GenBank No. ) is partially identical to D. discoideum MEK kinase alpha (GenBank No. ) [108]. It is possible that the serine/threonine kinase domain might phosphorylate the amoebal Noxes or the p67-like protein to stimulate ROS generation, analogous to other regulatory phosphorylations of Nox and their regulatory subunits [20,109-111]. Another interesting point of the Dd-PB1-A protein is to contain the F-box and a WD40 repeat regions that function as a ubiquitin ligase component E3. Further investigations to identify a binding partner will lead to understand functional relationships between Nox and the Dd-PB1 proteins.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 40 54 40 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. discoideum </italic>
###xml 0 70 0 70 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Predicted candidate binding partners of <italic>D. discoideum </italic>p67-like protein</bold>
###xml 191 203 191 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">parenthesis </italic>
###xml 40 53 <span type="species:ncbi:44689">D. discoideum</span>
Predicted candidate binding partners of D. discoideum p67-like protein. Predicted domain structures of Dd-p67-like protein and candidates of binding partners are shown. "basic" and "OPCA" in parenthesis indicate six characteristic residues of PB1 domain as shown in Figure 12. Abbreviations: kinase, protein serine/threonine kinase domain; F, F-box; WD40, WD40 repeat; WW, WW domain; ZZ, ZZ type zinc-finger.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
###xml 6 10 6 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
Do p67phox-like genes exist in plants?
###end title 79
###begin p 80
###xml 17 29 17 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 33 43 33 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. sativa </italic>
###xml 114 115 114 115 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 116 119 116 119 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B112">112</xref>
###xml 120 123 120 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B113">113</xref>
###xml 140 143 140 143 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B114">114</xref>
###xml 197 201 197 201 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 327 339 327 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 471 481 471 481 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. sativa </italic>
###xml 596 600 596 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 745 748 745 748 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B115">115</xref>
###xml 17 28 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 33 42 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">O. sativa</span>
###xml 327 338 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 471 480 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">O. sativa</span>
The land plants, A. thaliana and O. sativa possess the multiple EF-hand-containing Nox proteins, At-rboh-A to -J [1,112,113] and Os-rboh-A [114] to -H, respectively. However, there is no report of Phox-related regulatory subunit homologs in plant genomes. Unexpectedly BLAST search using PB1 domain sequences demonstrates that A. thaliana possesses a unique family of genes encoding four proteins that possess both TPR and PB1 domains (GenBank accession No. , , , ). The O. sativa genome also possesses a similar gene (GenBank accession No. ). Herein, we refer to this family as "hypothetical p67phox-like (hypo-p67-L)". The expressions of at least the two identified genes, At-hypo-p67-L1 and -L4, were confirmed according to the EST database [115].
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 25 37 25 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 41 51 41 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. sativa </italic>
###xml 91 94 91 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F14">14A</xref>
###xml 138 140 138 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S16">16</xref>
###xml 233 236 233 236 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F14">14A</xref>
###xml 279 281 279 281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S17">17</xref>
###xml 444 456 444 456 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 630 632 630 632 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S18">18</xref>
###xml 680 692 680 692 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 715 720 715 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 744 756 744 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 843 846 843 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F14">14B</xref>
###xml 913 918 913 918 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1021 1024 1021 1024 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fig" rid="F14">14B</xref>
###xml 1145 1147 1145 1147 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B10">10</xref>
###xml 25 36 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 41 50 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">O. sativa</span>
###xml 444 455 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 680 691 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 706 711 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 744 755 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 904 909 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Domain structures of the A. thaliana and O. sativa hypo-p67-L proteins are shown in Figure 14A (sequences are provided in Additional file 16). The six residues characteristic of the PB1 domains are conserved in all sequences (Figure 14A, and see the alignment in Additional file 17). This predicts that the hypo-p67-L proteins will form a heteromeric or homomeric complex via PB1-PB1-interaction. In addition to the hypo-p67-L gene family, the A. thaliana genome possessed at least 27 isolated genes encoding the PB1 domain [e.g. protein kinase family protein (GenBank No. ), CBSn-PB1 ortholog (GenBank No. ), see Additional file 18]. Alignment of putative AD-like domains of the A. thaliana proteins with human p67phox and NOXA1 show that the A. thaliana hypo-p67-L1 and -L2 proteins conserve the functionally critical valine residue (Figure 14B). Moreover, a lysine residue corresponding to Lys-196 of human p67phox that is correlated to the appearance of functional PB1 domain is also conserved in two of them (Figure 14B). On the other hand, the sequences do not conserve residues in the TPR domain known to be essential for binding to Rac [10]. Biological functions for this putative family are unknown and further investigations are needed.
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 13 19 13 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox- </italic>
###xml 0 49 0 49 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Predicted p67<italic>phox- </italic>like proteins in higher plants</bold>
###xml 102 106 102 106 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 164 176 164 176 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 180 189 180 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. sativa</italic>
###xml 204 219 204 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">F. graminearum </italic>
###xml 645 647 636 638 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="supplementary-material" rid="S17">17</xref>
###xml 650 656 641 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Boxes </italic>
###xml 745 749 736 740 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 765 776 756 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Underlines </italic>
###xml 164 175 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 180 189 <span type="species:ncbi:4530">O. sativa</span>
###xml 204 218 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">F. graminearum</span>
###xml 220 223 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">Fg-</span>
###xml 440 443 <span type="species:ncbi:5518">Fg-</span>
###xml 736 741 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Predicted p67phox- like proteins in higher plants. (A) Predicted domain structures of hypothetical p67phox-like proteins (At-hypo-p67-L1 to -L4, Os-hypo-p67-L1) of A. thaliana and O. sativa, and a fungal F. graminearum (Fg-) NOXR are shown, along with their GenBanktrade mark accession numbers. "basic" and "OPCA" in parenthesis indicate six characteristic residues of PB1 domains as shown in Figure 12. "D" and "R" below the TPR region of Fg-NOXR represent two conserved amino acid residues that are important for binding to Rac as indicated in Figure 5. (B) Alignments of the putative AD-like regions are shown (see details in Additional file 17). Boxes indicate lysine and valine residues corresponding to the Lys-196 and Val-204 of human p67phox, respectively. Underlines in alignment indicates amino acid with a hydropholic side group.
###end p 82
###begin title 83
Conclusion
###end title 83
###begin p 84
###xml 59 63 59 63 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 246 247 246 247 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 336 340 336 340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 344 348 344 348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 440 444 440 444 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 926 930 926 930 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Phox</italic>
###xml 1051 1055 1051 1055 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1064 1068 1064 1068 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1196 1200 1196 1200 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1209 1213 1209 1213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1289 1294 1289 1294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1307 1312 1307 1312 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1400 1411 1400 1411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">O. latipes </italic>
###xml 1432 1436 1432 1436 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1503 1508 1503 1508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1549 1554 1549 1554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1659 1664 1659 1664 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox </italic>
###xml 1806 1810 1806 1810 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 1400 1410 <span type="species:ncbi:8090">O. latipes</span>
###xml 2062 2067 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
In summary, we reported here an exhaustive analysis of the Phox-related regulatory subunits for Nox enzymes from a total of 32 species in the Eukaryota including 10 vertebrates. The present study, viewed in the context of the evolution of Noxes [1], reveals that regulatory subunits co-evolved with their respective Noxes; Nox2 with p67phox/p47phox; Nox1 with NOXO1/NOXA1; ancestral Nox2 as co-ortholog of vertebrate Nox1-3 with p67phox/p47phox-like proteins; fungal and amoebal NoxA/B with NOXR (and possibly new components). By comparing amino acid sequences of the regulatory subunits, putative key amino acid residues and conserved region previously undefined were identified, e.g. ADSIS. These conserved residues are likely to be important in conserved catalytic or regulatory functions of Nox proteins, although, the detailed biochemical roles of most of these residues are not yet fully understood. The analysis of the Phox-related regulatory subunits points to a novel evolutionary history of Nox regulatory proteins. The earliest Nox2 and p47phox- and p22phox-like genes are appearing in the unicellular choanoflagellate before the emergence of the metazoa. Duplication of primordial p47phox- and p67phox-like genes occurred in vertebrates, resulting in the emergence of NOXO1-p47phox and NOXA1-p67phox genes, respectively. Supporting this evolutionary origin, the NOXO1 protein in the fish O. latipes still retains the p47phox-characteristic "AIR". A predicted motif structure of ancestral p47phox suggests a greatly expanded family of p47phox including SH3PXD2 in the animal lineages. Detailed sequence analyses proposed an evolution model that p40phox originally participated in regulating both Nox1 and Nox2 in early vertebrates, but in mammals the regulation of Nox1 became independent of p40phox. Thus, this report provides keys to understand the evolutionary history of Nox and the regulatory subunits, and provides new information that may be useful in elucidating new molecular details of the activation mechanisms of Nox enzymes including the human orthologs.
###end p 84
###begin p 85
###xml 138 141 138 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="B116">116</xref>
###xml 399 411 399 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 453 465 453 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A. thaliana </italic>
###xml 468 472 468 472 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">phox</italic>
###xml 399 410 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
###xml 453 464 <span type="species:ncbi:3702">A. thaliana</span>
Note: While we were in the process of revising this manuscript, a review article about structure and function of the PB1 domain appeared [116]. The review will help to understand the structural features of the PB1 domain that are often mentioned in the present study. In the article, authors also described the presence of the hypothetical genes coding TPR and PB1 domain-containing proteins in the A. thaliana genomes and argued about a possibility of A. thaliana p67phox.
###end p 85
